From suraj at symonds.net  Mon Dec  2 09:21:48 2002
From: suraj at symonds.net (Suraj Kumar)
Date: 02 Dec 2002 14:51:48 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] Kernel modules on startup
In-Reply-To: <20021202090655.86159.qmail@web40602.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20021202090655.86159.qmail@web40602.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <1038820914.1691.58.camel@suraj.cybernetsoft.com>

On Mon, 2002-12-02 at 14:36, Rajkumar Gopalaswamy wrote:
>  i am using debian(woody). how do i reconfigure the
> kernel modules to be insmoded on startup. I configured

edit /etc/modules and add the names of the modules (just the module
name, not module_file.o)

> installing it, so they occupy lot of memory. I want it
> not to load some modules on startup. How can i
> proceed. thanks in advance.

The best solution is to make use of the update-modules script and
/etc/modutils/ directory. The update-modules(8) man page describes the
process very well.

  -Suraj

From suraj at symonds.net  Mon Dec  2 09:46:29 2002
From: suraj at symonds.net (Suraj Kumar)
Date: 02 Dec 2002 15:16:29 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] auto-logout in redhat 7.3
In-Reply-To: <1038821190.56a19300barani@myrealbox.com>
References: <1038821190.56a19300barani@myrealbox.com>
Message-ID: <1038822397.21115.63.camel@suraj.cybernetsoft.com>

On Mon, 2002-12-02 at 14:56, baranidharan pakkiriswamy wrote:
>       I am working on Redhat 7.3 .My system goes to 
> log out automatically after some 15 min every time i login .i didnt set anywhere 15 min for logout .
> can anyone tell me how to get rid off this problem ?

Is this from the console login that you are talking about? If yes, it
could be because you have the TMOUT variable set to 900 (which is the
seconds equivalent of 15 mins). But I doubt thats redhat 7.3's default
feature.

If its the graphical environment, look at your graphical environment's
settings.

you hv not mentioned clearly whether this happens in your X Window session
or

if it is in a console session

$~ echo $TMOUT

if it is set
then unset this variable.

does this happen even if you are not idle (no kbd operation). ?

From srikanthns at vsnl.net  Mon Dec  2 13:13:42 2002
From: srikanthns at vsnl.net (N S Srikanth)
Date: Mon, 2 Dec 2002 18:43:42 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] Insatalling MDK 9 in Windows partition
References: <F26WNaBJjvmZp0mmhQZ00001599@hotmail.com>
Message-ID: <008001c29a07$a7fe3aa0$5fa841db@k>

Hi
If the E or F drive is free, you can dedicate that partition to MDK and you
can install without distrubing windows. No need for FAT 32 format
installation.During MDK installation point to that drive having free space
(E or F) and choose "Auto allocate" . You are done. It will not disturb
windows unless otherwise you choose that partition. It will use ext3 format

N S Srikanth

From prakash at cmi.ac.in  Tue Dec  3 04:38:06 2002
From: prakash at cmi.ac.in (Prakash Chandrasekaran)
Date: Tue, 3 Dec 2002 10:08:06 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] Insatalling MDK 9 in Windows partition
In-Reply-To: <F26WNaBJjvmZp0mmhQZ00001599@hotmail.com>
References: <F26WNaBJjvmZp0mmhQZ00001599@hotmail.com>
Message-ID: <20021203043806.GA1329@cmi.ac.in>

On Mon, Dec 02, 2002 at 11:39:44AM +0000, Dhanagopal Rengasamy wrote:
> 
> 
> I would like to go for Mandrake 9.0 linux for windows without disturbing 
> the existing settings.
> As per thier insturctions, Mandrake linux fow windows can be installed in a 
> window partition in a separate folder.

	Under this option an ext3 (assuming you use ext3 for Linux) image file
will be created under the FAT-32 partition, and this image will be used instead
of a disk partition. But, this results in performance loss, and also you are 
leaving your entire Linux installation (ie. the filesystem image) at the mercy 
of windows. If your FAT-32 filesystem gets corrupted, then the image file (and 
thereby your linux installation) is also screwed.


> Is it possible to install MDK without losing any data in my E or F 
> partition? if it is installed
> in windows, will it use FAT-32 or ext.3 File system?
> 

	These have already been answered. So, there's nothing more to say.

On Mon, 2002-12-02 at 23:31, R.Dhanagopal wrote:
> I would like to know the number of Linux users in and around Pondicherry 
> (home / office / business /College etc) to form a GNU/Linux User Group 
> with the participation of like minded persons for better interaction and mutual 
> co-operation.  I request the interested persons to provide me their email id 
> along with their address, and telephone number. If you know anybody in Pondicherry
> interested in Linux, kindIy forward this message to them. 

all the best to your efforts. :)

If you are thinking of starting a user group for all sorts of  free
software (that could be *BSD, GNU/*, or even Apache / X / whatever)
consider starting an FSUG. Contact gnu@gnu.org.in and find out how you
can start an FSUG in your area. In brief, an FSUG will not only give
technical support for Free Software users but will also discourage the
use of non-free software. If you think it is important that people
should realise the ills of non-free software consider starting an FSUG.
A GLUG (GNU/Linux User Group) would be fine too but that will narrow
down the users in your group (as was said earlier, *BSD, GNU/^(linux)
users may not be interested). I would personally discourage forming a
"LUG".

 
> What is Linux
> 
> Linux is another operating system like windows95/98/2000/XP.  The good

Dhanagopal, please do consider finding out more about Linux and the GNU:

  http://gnu.org/gnu/linux-and-gnu.html

> thing about Linux is it is easy to use and extremely reliable and
> powerfull. Linux is free to use & it is legal to share with your
> friends and is ideally suited for people like us in India. This comes
> bundled with all the necessary software for doing most of the things.
> No need to buy any extra software,  

I bet you will find most of your friends "complaining" that it is not
easy to install. The issue is not about ease of use. Its not about power
either. There are more powerful / easy to use proprietary OSes, Software
available. GNU/Linux stands out in the fact that it gives you the
freedom to do anything with it.

> Come on. How come your Linux is powerful and still free? legal to
> share? 

Its powerful because its free :) (free as in swatantra, suthanthiram (or
as Mr.P.Asokan suggests - 'Thal(2)aiyaru Menkalam')).

  -suraj

there are HTML editors for Linux but i'm afraid there aren't any great 
WYSIWYG tools that can be an alternative to Dreamweaver. :-(

But u have some widget-based really good HTML editor's - really worth 
giving a try

check out

Bluefish(i've worked with it) (GPL) - very similar to "Screem"(i've only 
seen screenshots)

http://bluefish.openoffice.nl/index.php

Both "Bluefish" and "Screem" are NOT visual tools. They are HTML Text 
editors. But then u dont have to write much. These come along with 
plenty of widgets.

The best WYSIWYG/Visual tools for creating HTML content that i've seen 
yet are
Mozilla's Composer component and
OpenOffice's Writer(stretching tables/columns around are quite easy here).

i haven't come across a real equivalent yet! let me know if u do.

regards,
ramesh pallikara

From sriram.narayanan at polaris.co.in  Tue Dec  3 08:19:57 2002
From: sriram.narayanan at polaris.co.in (sriram.narayanan@polaris.co.in)
Date: Tue, 3 Dec 2002 13:49:57 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] Insatalling Linux in Windows partition
Message-ID: <OFCBEE5955.9283EF04-ON65256C84.002D5E88@polaris.co.in>

This is a multi-part message in MIME format.

------=_NextPartTM-000-27b9f158-0689-11d7-b295-00b0d0688b56
Content-type: text/plain; charset=us-ascii


Hi,

It's fairly simple. There should not be any problem with RH 8.0 Dual boot
Windoz,

Install Windows 2000 Server of Windows '98 leaving apart not less than 6 GB
if you intend to install everything available in RH 8.0.

Once the Installation is completed, Boot with the RH 8.0 CD and in the Disk
Partition Option choose Manual and Opt for Disk Drud

Create Partitions for Linux Swap (Minimum Double the Size of your System
RAM) then balance for \ or as desired by you for \usr \temp \var, etc....

Since the Linux Boot cannot be put before the 1024 Cylinders, it would
prompt you to create a Boot Disk (create it for safety reasons), choose
GRUB as the Boot Loader. The rest will be taken care by the Installation
Wizard.

Enjoy Linux...

Thanx
-Sriram

Message-ID: <001f01c29adc$99540c20$7da841db@k>

From: "R.Dhanagopal" <dhanagopal_r@hotmail.com>
To: "N S Srikanth" <srikanthns@vsnl.net>
Cc: <ilugc@aero.iitm.ernet.in>
Sent: Monday, December 02, 2002 10:16 PM
Subject: Re: [Ilugc] Insatalling MDK 9 in Windows partition


> Dear Srikanth
>
> Thanks for your reply.  If I install MDK in E or F partition, there will
be
> 3 OSes in the system (Windoze, RH7.2 and MDK9). Lilo is the bootloader
now.
> After installing MDK9, should I make any changes in the lilo-config file
for
> the proper display of the names of all the 3 OSes while booting?

Install MDK and install boot loader lilo in the first sector of boot
partition of MDK installation. Boot through the boot disk created during MDK
installation, boot into MDK and see the entries in /etc/lilo.conf. Put those
entries in the "other" column in the /etc/lilo.conf file of your present RH
7.2 installation. Run "lilo -v ".
Reboot the machine. Now you should see the 3 entries : Dos, Linux, Mandrake.
Choose the system boot into
> In another system WinXP and RH7.3 are installed with GRUB bootloader.
> Suppose if I install MDK9 now in an empty partition, what changes I should
> make in the GRUB-config file. How much mininum space is needed for the
> typical MDK9 installation?
>
> R.Dhanagopal
A minmum of 4GB is needed IMHO

N S Srikanth

In-Reply-To: <20021204114012.48649.qmail@web40602.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20021204114012.48649.qmail@web40602.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <200212041243.SAA30403@hd2.dot.net.in>

Hello,

>   Which of the filesytems ext3, reiserfs and xfs is
> the best ? In terms of performance, data transfer
> speed, data reliability, security, recovery from power
> failures, etc...

The "best" really dfepends on what you want it to do. I've been using ext3 
for a while now on my desktop machines with no issues, and afaik, ext3 is 
just a jounalling layer on top of ext2, so conversion may be easier...

ReiserFS seems to be best for a large number of small files.

I you have large files (ours are usually mangy GB in size, and we have 
hundreds of those), go with XFS. Its very well designed, superb data transfer 
speeds. I have pulled the power plug, literally (bad me :) on a production 
machine running XFS, and it comes back online without any problems. I have 
had no problems with its reliability. And feature wise, it would still be the 
best (for me, that is). For instance it supports ACL's and extended 
attributes. So ACL's would take care of micro level of security for you (if 
you want extreme security go for an encrypted fs). Extended attributes, are 
system and user definable attributes that are stored with the inode info. For 
example, our playout system verfies if each file is a legal video file (as in 
data format, you don't want somebody cat random_garbage > file.dv and send it 
on air) and marks it as suitable for playout. This is stored as an extended 
attribute by a daemon. The playout machines check the attribs to see if the 
files are production ready. In fact, ACL's are stored in the system part of 
the EA. A simpler usage of these might be id tags for your mp3 collection 
stored in the EA. So searching is very fast on all tag info (I used to do 
this on the BeOS), and if you have several thousand files, its invaulable... 
Before I get micro flamed for using the non-free mp3 format, lets me state 
you can use it for ogg too :) or pretty much anything...  

The latest release candidate is on the sgi site : 

http://oss.sgi.com/projects/xfs

regards
BGa
-- 
We will find a way, or we will make one - Hannibal

> Dear Srikanth
>
> Thanks for your reply.  If I install MDK in E or F partition, there will
be
> 3 OSes in the system (Windoze, RH7.2 and MDK9). Lilo is the bootloader
now.
> After installing MDK9, should I make any changes in the lilo-config file
for
> the proper display of the names of all the 3 OSes while booting?

Following the above thread, I am giving below my /etc/lilo.conf

prompt
timeout=50
default=DOS
boot=/dev/hda
map=/boot/map
install=/boot/boot.b
message=/boot/message
lba32

image=/boot/vmlinuz-2.4.18-3
 label=linux
 initrd=/boot/initrd-2.4.18-3.img
 read-only
 root=/dev/hda9
 append="hdc=ide-scsi"

other=/dev/hda1
 optional
 label=DOS

other=/dev/hda11
       optional
       label=Mandrake

This is the /etc/lilo.conf  in Redhat 7.3 installation .First Win 98, then I
installed RH 7.3 and then  I installed MDK 9.0 afterwards in a 5 GB
partition carved out of windows partition.

HTH

N S Srikanth

From prabhu at aero.iitm.ernet.in  Thu Dec  5 04:12:43 2002
From: prabhu at aero.iitm.ernet.in (Prabhu Ramachandran)
Date: Thu, 5 Dec 2002 09:42:43 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] Python needed
In-Reply-To: <001201c29bfd$38eecb00$56ab09ca@godcaresme>
References: <001201c29bfd$38eecb00$56ab09ca@godcaresme>
Message-ID: <15854.53819.131904.622457@monster.linux.in>

>>>>> "Thiagu" == thiaguwin  <Thiagarajan> writes:

    Thiagu> Good Morning !  i want to learn phthon, Can i get python
    Thiagu> cd and its documentation ?

If you are running any Linux^W GNU/Linux ;) distro worth its salt
(Debian, RH, Mdk, Slackware etc.)  install the Python binaries (rpms,
debs whatever) and the python docs.  Under Debian its called
python-doc.  This contains a tutorial, the library reference and a
whole bunch of other docs that are of great use.  I recommend starting
with the tutorial.  These docs are also available online at
http://www.python.org/ .

If you want to buy/download a book look here:

 http://www.python.org/doc/

There are *lots* of resources both online and in dead-tree form.

You might also want to read this:

http://www.onlamp.com/pub/a/python/2001/02/07/pythonnews.html

and this:

http://www.andamooka.org/

It has a "Non Programmer's Tutorial For Python".

On Windows the Python installer ships with all the standard Python
docs that you can choose to install.

cheers,
prabhu

hello,

Thiagarajan wanted us to know:

> Good Morning
> Kindly Clarify Why Images are always in rectange form in computer graphics ?
> Is it possible to make in any form ?, i need it for an application
> for some of you this may be a simple question.
> i have searched using the search engine's but fail to get suitable reply.
> kindly reply or give reference
> have a nice day

I guess this is because traditional GUIs have been rectangular. Win32
API does have some polygon functions, but its hard. (IIRC, ICQ99 had a
round startup window)

Anyways, these 'irregular' windows were just a hack. You have to remove
each pixel individually, and also remove mouse sensitivity within those
areas. Even then, there were some visual glitches, like when you move
the window, the frame is still rectangular.

This was all sometime win98-ish, when I used to program as a child.
Things might have changed now. (Win2K has some nice Alpha blending
functions)
 
For now, you could live with transparency. Thats the closest you can
get.

	-- Ganesh

Hi Suraj,
    What are the books you are expecting? if it is on programming
    which programming language you prefer?
   
    For me natural thing to introduce is functional programming.
    functional programming is "The" programming. We don't need
    to mud their mind with pointers and other implementation
    issues. there are many good books on functional programming.
    My preference is "sicp" structure and interpretation of
    computer programming. Instead of duplicating the work we
    can convince author/publisher to publish an indian editon.

    There are some good books  on  functional programming in
    general and Hakell in particular. Walder and Bird comes to
    my mind.

    One advantage of teaching hakell kind of languages is it is
    close to their class mathematics. 

    one question to the list. What is your first algorithm?

regards,
Sam

Thiagarajan wanted us to know:

> Good Morning Mr. Ganesh Swami !
> Thank you for your prompt reply

> from your reply i am able to get the message " Till date ,computers can
> create images only in rectangular base" is that the meaning ?.

Close. Necessity is the mother of all inventions. 

UI gurus have only been thinking about rectangular UI objects. There
hasn't been a need for irregular objects.

Tell me why you would want an irregular image.

Its much easier to store just four coods (x1,y1,x2,y2) instead of
numerous points along the border.

<!-- insert arguments about vector and raster stuff -->

A simple example. The mouse pointer is not a rectangle. But, if you open
the XBM or ICO (or CUR) file in a suitable editor, you will find that it
is rectangular. With some simple tricks (XOR), you can get any shape
you want. 

> is it not possible to make fundamental changes in the OS itsef ?.

What has the OS got to do with this ?

> is it not possible to make a new format of image where the base is not a
> rectangel ?

Sure, it is possible. But think of the amount of information you've got 
to store about each pixel. The best (and only) approach is to stick with
transparency. Transparency with layering (flat) can be neat.

From vvikram at Stanford.EDU  Sun Dec  8 07:14:30 2002
From: vvikram at Stanford.EDU (Vikram)
Date: Sat, 7 Dec 2002 23:14:30 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT] Images only in Rectangle ?
In-Reply-To: <20021208071250.GA13798@ganesh.gslabs>
Message-ID: <Pine.GSO.4.44.0212072310170.13971-100000@elaine18.Stanford.EDU>

yes, there is something to add here. the problem is clearly not the
question of rectangular objects or UI-lameness though it surely
is a factor. the real issue is you are always interpolating a
2d real coordinate system [your image] to a 2d integer coordinate
system [your screen]. the loss of precision here can be offset
cleverly in many ways namely anti-aliasing, shading etc. of course
increasing the granularity of what we call a `pixel` is really the
best way to get around such interpolative errors and thats why
as resolution increases your images appear sharper, better and more
"dense". taking this argument , at a more fundamental level its a
problem between analog [nature] and discrete [computer] domains. its
really the reason why we have to "sample" signals to feed into
"digital signal processors" [computers].

its a lot of math and i think foley, van damme [sp?] introduction to
graphics is a good book to start out with.

thanks. regards,
			Vikram

From Ravi Rao <mail at ravirao.net>  Sun Dec  8 09:49:23 2002
From: Ravi Rao <mail at ravirao.net> (Ravi Rao)
Date: Sun, 8 Dec 2002 04:49:23 -0500
Subject: [Ilugc] opensource ???
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0212081422060.23849-100000@mrna.tn.nic.in>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0212081422060.23849-100000@mrna.tn.nic.in>
Message-ID: <20021208094923.GA6650@symonds.net>

Hi,

* km@mrna.tn.nic.in <km@mrna.tn.nic.in> [Sun, Dec 08, 2002 at 02:22:48PM +0530]:

KM> whats the difference between the GNU/linux distros offered on the web for
KM> download(isos,i386s etc) to those offered as packages on a commercial
KM> basis (eg : Red hat Professional edition) ?  and why is that the

	The boxed set comes with "powertools" and other "goodies" that are
not shipped as a part of the regular ISO. Some call it "extras" as well. You
can have extra editors, graphics software, 3d image rendering software,
VariCAD, and other stuff in those CDs. They might also include extra printed
manuals, in multiple languages, and 30-day, or 3 month technical support,
and stickers, and other spam^W flyers, brochures etc.

KM> commercial editions  cost  so high  inspite of GNU/linux an opensource ?

	Because "opensource" does not mean "free as in beer".
	
	It only means you can peek at the sourcecode if you want. And if
appropriately licensed, play around with it, the way you want.

	See http://www.fsf.org/philosophy/free-software-for-freedom.html

	Pls don't send multiple copies of email to the list.

	thanks,

		--ravi.

From suraj at symonds.net  Sun Dec  8 11:04:54 2002
From: suraj at symonds.net (Suraj Kumar)
Date: Sun, 8 Dec 2002 16:34:54 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] [demo-schools] book writers?
In-Reply-To: <20021208084950.53638.qmail@web12206.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.3.96.1021207175600.29797A-100000@macaque.cmi.ac.in> <20021208084950.53638.qmail@web12206.mail.yahoo.com>

[WARNING: Cross posted]

hi sanjay, D@S team and others,

Sanjay Chigurupati wrote on Sun, Dec 08, 2002 at 12:49:50AM -0800: 

,----[ on the issue of writing books ]
| what topics are you looking at? what is the audience you are looking
| at, with respect to their familiarity of the topic?
`----

The audience  is school students (also  college students if  we grow a
bit further). Practically, the students that we met seem to know a lot
more than  what we (or atleast  me) expected. Though on  the topics of
fundamentals of computing, fundamentals of programming, they are a bit
weak. Most still  think the 'start' button is due  to some chip inside
their computer. :) Yet they seem to know most of the 'practical' stuff
like browsing the WWW, using yahoo, etc., :)

We have the following plans:

a. Review /  Rework / Modify  Jonathan Bartlett's book  - "Programming
Ground Up". This book is more  of an introduction to programming for a
mature user (using assembly as its main form of teaching techniques in
programming).  We haven't  started the review yet, but  i find it very
good. This  could be something we  can take to  colleges. [*]

b. Our primary aim is to tell the schools that Free Software education
is viable  and that we can  support them frame  their syllabus, books,
etc.,.  The  bruises that  our friends from  the FSUGs got  from their
effort in the  kerala government's IT@SCHOOLS project is  a lesson for
us and we will have to make  sure we have all the books in hand before
we go for  a proposal to, say, an individual  school or the government
of Tamil  Nadu. Hence we  write new books  / modify existing  books to
make sure we give them enough infrastructure.

c. Currently these are our plans:

1. Arun (Kochi)  will write a  book on 'Introduction to  the GNU/Linux
system'.  Target audience: 6th standard [**]

2. Manikandan  is  thinking of  writing  a  book  on 'Fundamentals  of
Networking'.    We   would   use   MKS's  existing   work   for   this
purpose. Target Audience: 10th - 12th. [+]

3. I  just  started  out  on   writing  a  book  on  'Fundamentals  of
Computers'. Target audience: 4th standard. [*]

4. Jonathan Bartlett's 'Programming Ground up'  - yet to decide how we
can  use  this. I  guess  only college  students  can  take this,  not
schoolers.

5. stuff  from  gnupress.org,  etc.,  need  to  be  trimmed  and  made
dilute. save work as much as possible.

  Take a look at these from:

	     http://gpasokan.com/demo-schools/cvs/books/

(
Legend: 

[*] - compiled form of the book isn't available yet (maybe we will put
them up on the downloads section on savannah, not in the repository). 

[**] - pre development stage! 

[+] - planning stage - yet to commence writing

)

It would  be very  helpful if  people here can  come forward  to write
simple books (maybe 90 page stuff - typically like what the govt of TN
writes).  Topics could  be anything that you think  kids need to learn
about computing and  Free Software. Like with the  FSUG-Kochi guys, we
are trying to make sure that we dont teach just one particular product
(like, not  just GNOME when it  comes to a desktop,  but genrally talk
about  what  an  'icon'  is  and  what minimising  a  window  is  with
references to GNOME,  KDE, WMAKER, etc.,). Your work  must be released
under the terms of the GNU FDL (http://gnu.org/licenses/fdl.txt).

Join the demo@schools mailing list  and pour your suggestions. tell us
how you can help us. 

      http://gpasokan.com/cgi-bin/mailman/listinfo/demo-schools

Note: You can borrow the existing computer books proposed by the Tamil
Nadu State  Board for classes 11th,  12th from me  (ph: 2233483) (also
available at most book stores)

  -Suraj

From smohan at vsnl.com  Mon Dec  9 01:38:45 2002
From: smohan at vsnl.com (S Mohan)
Date: Mon, 9 Dec 2002 07:08:45 +0530
Subject: [ilugc] Windows XP, RH-8 and MDK-9- GRUB bootloader problem
In-Reply-To: <DAV51zubLR95CBUzN8I0000850f@hotmail.com>
Message-ID: <001101c29f23$b8080400$a46041db@18yamuna>

First. Please send posts in plaintext and not HTML.

I'm assuming GRUB is installed in the MBR after installing Linux and
hence points to the Linux 8.0 partition. If you have the Linux emergency
disk, you can boot with that and reinstall grub on the MBR. The GRUB
menu is in /boot/grub. While installing Mandrake, the bootsector must
have been loaded in that partition itself like you did for Linux. The
grub boot specification must point to that partition in that menu entry
for Mandrake.

Mohan

From smohan at vsnl.com  Mon Dec  9 01:57:54 2002
From: smohan at vsnl.com (S Mohan)
Date: Mon, 9 Dec 2002 07:27:54 +0530
Subject: [ilugc] Windows XP, RH-8 and MDK-9- GRUB bootloader problem
In-Reply-To: <DAV51zubLR95CBUzN8I0000850f@hotmail.com>
Message-ID: <000001c29f26$64997f30$a46041db@18yamuna>

Sorry. I did not read the mail fully while replying. In case Redhat is
giving problem with boot from floppy, what are those errors? My guess is
that while installing Mandrake, you may not have installed the boot
sector on the same partition.

To fix this, you need to execute fdisk /mbr from the Windows boot floppy
- dos mode. This will make the system boot from Windows default.
Mandrake can be booted from floppy anyway. If the Redhat boot problem is
due to floppy corruption, you would not have problems. Boot Mandrake,
mount the Redhat partition and check the menu.lst or grub.conf file.
Copy the menu portion pointing to Redhat to the Mandrake grub.conf. Boot
with mdk floppy and see if all the boots go thro' properly. Then issue
grub-install /dev/hda.

Mohan

the "make install" part will matter if not root and without the prefix
to configure.

XFree.

From sriram at aero.iitm.ernet.in  Mon Dec  9 05:14:33 2002
From: sriram at aero.iitm.ernet.in (P. Sriram)
Date: Mon, 9 Dec 2002 10:44:33 +0530 (IST)
Subject: [Ilugc] NIS Password problem on client end
In-Reply-To: <20021204181001.M81497@mail.kongu.ac.in>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0212091040180.11292-100000@gateway.aero.iitm.ernet.in>

On Wed, 4 Dec 2002, Arvind Kalyan wrote:
[in reply to nis problem]
> > I'm running NIS Server on Redhat6.2. I've created 7 users in NIS Server 
> m/c. and I've created directories for the users with their name as the  login 
> id on the client end(nis clients) . Now I've changed the password for a user 
> in NIS Server m/c and the thing is I'm still able to login with the old 
> password of the user from the client end. 

[etc etc and the solution was]
> 1) cd /var/yp
> 2) make
> now u can use the new password on all the systems. alternatively, use 
> the 'yppasswd' to change the password on the NIS server.
> To use yppasswd, start the yppasswdd server.

or, better yet, upgrade to a newer version of the os. nis is one of the
things that is partially broken in older versions of red hat. it works
much better in 7.2 and later. also, with these later versions, there is no
need to use yppasswd on the client - pam is set up so that if nis is
enabled, the usual passwd command will work like yppasswd (you will need 
to run yppasswdd on the server, of course). also, this business of running 
a make in /var/yp will not be needed.

sriram

You can use webmin. It is great. I've been using it for over 3 years now.
However, it still does not take away the fact that you need to know what you
are doing. If not, even with the GUI, you can land up with a wrong/bad
configuration. Further, if you learn how to tune sendmail.mc, you could use
options not available in webmin e.g. smtp authentication.

Mohan

From Udaya Kumar.R" <uk_ci at yahoo.com  Mon Dec  9 14:11:51 2002
From: Udaya Kumar.R" <uk_ci at yahoo.com (Udaya kumar.R)
Date: Mon, 9 Dec 2002 19:41:51 +0530 (IST)
Subject: [Ilugc] xfs
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0212082026140.24525-100000@mrna.tn.nic.in>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0212091931490.1358-100000@Uday.bksys.co.in>

Hi ,

   I was just checking xfs some time back. I could help you with what i
remember.

Choose XFS for large filesystems, which would contain large files.
Choose ReiserFS for smaller filesystems , which would contain small files.

If you are not sure of the above, better stay with EXT3, which is in
between XFS and ReiserFS.

I too remember of a site which gave me some comparison chart. But it seems
my poor memory couldn't help it. Probably you can google for it.

  From that rating i understood that XFS is for large files which wont get
added/removed frequently,ReiserFs is for small files which would be 
added/removed frequently. And EXT3 as usuall performed moderately well 
with most of the tests.

   Hope this helps.
Bye and take care.
uday.

> what if its on a web server ?

Webservers usually have large number of small files, and XFS won't give you 
any advantages there (though I doubt if there will be any degradation of 
performance). Again, if you have a few hyndred thousand fles the inode 
managementin XFS will be useful...

You cannot be a kernel user.  Anyway, I think that you meant GNU/Linux

read (http://www.gnu.org/gnu/why-gnu-linux.html).

The 5  CD set of which the  last 2 CDs contain  `non-free' stuff.  You
should  be very  careful when  using  `non-free' stuff  and this  gets
magnified when you  start deploying apps.  You may land  up in a legal
tangle if you are  going to install those apps for a  3rd Party !  All
said and done, `non-free' stuff is  an evil thing because it keeps the
community divided and  helpless.  Why go along with  such things which
does not guarantee your `swathanthriyam' ?


>> one more  thing is that  any body  know how the  core of the  OS is
>> compiled and run or tested ? 

Some say that the core of an OS is the kernel.  But you will find that
other components which make up an OS are equally critical.

Here, the  source code of  the kernel Linux  can be patched  using the
patch command  and updated to a  later version.  You  can compile this
kernel for your hardware and  device needs and get better performance.
Please read the relevant Kernel  Compiling HOWTO which can be got from
(ftp://www.ibiblio.org/pub/Linux/docs/HOWTO/).

Do get  back to this  List when you  have pointed doubts and  we shall
help you help yourself.

From hari at mae.ufl.edu  Tue Dec 10 03:13:12 2002
From: hari at mae.ufl.edu (Srihari Rasmi)
Date: Tue, 10 Dec 2002 08:43:12 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT] Images only in Rectangle ?
References: <Pine.GSO.4.44.0212072310170.13971-100000@elaine18.Stanford.EDU>
Message-ID: <3DF55BC8.6020709@mae.ufl.edu>

Vikram wrote:
> yes, there is something to add here. the problem is clearly not the
> question of rectangular objects or UI-lameness though it surely
> is a factor. 

Please...the rectangular object _is_ the issue. And its _not_ 
UI-lameness...its the UI's simplicity. Keeping things simple has always 
been the key. Contrary to intuition...a rectangle needs only four 
variables i.e., (x_1,y_1),(x_1,y_2),(x_2,y_1),(x_2,y_2). Even a 
quadrilateral would need eight variables i.e (x_i,y_i); 0<i<5; i belongs 
to N.
'Fractally', the pixel is a rectangle. Its easy to build an exact huge 
rectangle out of small rectangles. No matter how small the pixels, you 
cant build an exact triangle.

[OT] When things come to windows, mouse sensitivity within a window 
needs only one parameter specifying the boundary (the horizontal bound 
or the vertical) when the mouse is moving in a straight line along _any_ 
direction...this is very simple. But think about a quadrilateral...you 
would need to specify the slope _and_ an initial starting point for the 
boundary line...which means...we need two parameters. More 
complex...lets stay simple.

 > the real issue is you are always interpolating a
 > 2d real coordinate system [your image] to a 2d integer coordinate
 > system [your screen]. the loss of precision here can be offset
 > cleverly in many ways namely anti-aliasing, shading etc.

I dont see how this is relevant to the topic of rectangular images.
[OT] _Every_ image is sampled (digitised). Even our eye does this.
There are two issues involved here 1) the bit rate..or depth resolution, 
and 2) the screen resolution. The more of both...the better.
There is _no_ interpolation anywhere! There is only truncation involved. 
  For eg., draw a one-pixel thick straight line, with a slope, in an 
losslessly compressed or uncompressed format...say .png...and see the 
effect of resizing this image in a browser window. This should explain 
truncation.
And Anti-aliasing was brought in because our eyes do a lousy job at 
sampling...and because the computer monitor has a fixed screen resolution.

of course
> increasing the granularity of what we call a `pixel` is really the
> best way to get around such interpolative errors and thats why
> as resolution increases your images appear sharper, better and more
> "dense". taking this argument , at a more fundamental level its a
> problem between analog [nature] and discrete [computer] domains. its
> really the reason why we have to "sample" signals to feed into
> "digital signal processors" [computers].

One can never know the difference between the analog and discrete. We 
always 'see' digital. The eye does a spatial sampling (a frame) and a 
time sampling (movie). What we see is a movie played at approx. 30 
frames per sec.
So...the real problem is how to make things discrete so that its more 
acceptable and pleasing for us (for eg. anti-aliasing).

>>>from your reply i am able to get the message " Till date ,computers can
>>>create images only in rectangular base" is that the meaning ?.
>>
>>Close. Necessity is the mother of all inventions.
>>
>>UI gurus have only been thinking about rectangular UI objects. There
>>hasn't been a need for irregular objects.
>>
>>Tell me why you would want an irregular image.

Exactly.

>>>is it not possible to make a new format of image where the base is not a
>>>rectangel ?
>>
>>Sure, it is possible. But think of the amount of information you've got
>>to store about each pixel. The best (and only) approach is to stick with
>>transparency. Transparency with layering (flat) can be neat.

That is precisely why transparency was brought in.

>>Do you want an (Textual) Image Viewer ? Please
>>elaborate.

Is there anything like a textual image viewer??? Its difficult for me to 
comprehend how this would work. Any references/links?

Now...coming to images...as to why things are easy when they are 
rectangular. They key is this: the encoding of an image is very orderly 
when a rectagle is maintained. _Any_ image encoder exploits this.
As mentioned before, if an 'irregular' image is needed, specify the 
necessary pixels to have 100% transparency (called alpha in most cases). 
I dont think JPEG can do this...any decent lossless compression scheme 
like PNG has transparency.

Hari

On Tue, Dec 10, 2002 at 08:43:12AM +0530, Srihari Rasmi wrote:
> Vikram wrote:

> variables i.e., (x_1,y_1),(x_1,y_2),(x_2,y_1),(x_2,y_2). Even a

A nitpick:
A rectangle needs only two points = 4 variables.
Assuming that the vertices are numbered continuously,
(x1, y1) + (x3, y3) or (x2, y2) + (x4, y4) is enough.

> 'Fractally', the pixel is a rectangle. Its easy to build an exact huge 
> rectangle out of small rectangles. No matter how small the pixels, you 
> cant build an exact triangle.
This also equates to 'analog' vs 'digital' in some fashion.

> 
> [OT] When things come to windows, mouse sensitivity within a window 
> needs only one parameter specifying the boundary (the horizontal bound 
> or the vertical) when the mouse is moving in a straight line along _any_ 
> direction...this is very simple. But think about a quadrilateral...you 
> would need to specify the slope _and_ an initial starting point for the 
> boundary line...which means...we need two parameters. More 
> complex...lets stay simple.
Thats why the underlying 'bounding rectangle' is always used. IOW
whatever be the visual shape the system treats it as a rectangle
- technically the smallest rectangle with its edges parallel to the
screen that contains the shape.
> 
[snip]
> 
> That is precisely why transparency was brought in.
> 
> >>Do you want an (Textual) Image Viewer ? Please
> >>elaborate.
> 
> Is there anything like a textual image viewer??? Its difficult for me to 
> comprehend how this would work. Any references/links?
I do not know if it really qualifies as a `text image viewer' but
zgv (or any other svgalib centric program) can display an image
without the necessity of X running.

hello,

rh bala wanted us to know:

> my name is balachandar.M
> 
> and i am a linux user and i am in need of newest version(8.0) linux 
> consisting of 5 CDS.

Linux^WGNU/Linux (srs, I am a quick learner ;)) is usually
"distributed". The one you are referring to is called Redhat. And, you
dont need CDs 4 and 5. Read the other threads.

> one more thing is that any body know how the core of the OS is compiled 
> and run or tested? if so then reply me plz.....

The core of _your_ OS is the kernel, and its called Linux. The userspace is
from GNU and many operating systems share these tools, simply because
they are the best. eg: FreeBSD, "Linux", etc..

The kernel is compiled just like a normal program. Since Linux is a
monolithic (pseudo maybe ?) one, its a single, huge chunk.

Many projects (FreeBSD, GNOME) use a "build sheriff", which continuously
builds the CVS, and when it breaks, it sends an email to the
maintainers. Thats a good way to keep the CVS in a buildable state.
IIRC, GNOME uses Tinderbox.

Testing is done by humans. Linux is released very often (Oh no! not
another release). 

If you like receiving email (I do), I suggest subscribing to the
linux-kernel mailing list. It maybe an overkill at start. You have been
warned !

One stop solution (easier than Google)
http://loll.sf.net/ 

	Ganesh

>>>>> "SR" == Srihari Rasmi <hari@mae.ufl.edu> writes:

    SR> One can never know the difference between the analog and
    SR> discrete. We always 'see' digital. The eye does a spatial
    SR> sampling (a frame) and a time sampling (movie). What we see is
    SR> a movie played at approx. 30 frames per sec.  So...the real

Well, this is OT but what the heck, actually, you never really 'see'
what your eyes see.  You see a projected and interpolated/extrapolated
version of what your brain (mind whichever you believe) creates using
what the eye sees.  This is the scientific view.  Forget the
philosophical standpoints.  "Seeing" is way more complex than just
imaging a rasterized image.

cheers,
prabhu

>    6. Re: i need a linux 8.0 5 CDs immediately plz (Ganesh Swami)

Noticed this in the recent subject-lines of ILUGC. One optimum way of
sharing distros could be to set up a CD Repository. We, in Goa, make it a
point to buy one copy of the latest distros (say from linuxplaza.org or
from lincds.com) and then pass it around to as many people who want to
copy it. This way, the distro gets 'life' of its own, and there are enough
copies floating around our small state for anyone to get access to when
required. Of course, it calls for a small initial investment, of around Rs
35 to 50 per CD. Not a big price to promote GNU/Linux perhaps! The idea is
catching on, and we're trying to promote it among Little League LUGs (the
smaller groups) in places like Mangalore, Pondicherry and Belgaum. FN

> Noticed this in the recent subject-lines of ILUGC. One optimum way of
> sharing distros could be to set up a CD Repository. We, in Goa, make it a
> point to buy one copy of the latest distros (say from linuxplaza.org or
> from lincds.com) and then pass it around to as many people who want to
> copy it. This way, the distro gets 'life' of its own, and there are enough
> copies floating around our small state for anyone to get access to when
> required. Of course, it calls for a small initial investment, of around Rs
> 35 to 50 per CD. Not a big price to promote GNU/Linux perhaps! The idea is
> catching on, and we're trying to promote it among Little League LUGs (the

think about it.

everyday i hear __extremely___ intelligent people say 'oh linux. that geek
system', 'oh linux, yeah i tried it man and some guy came after me for
making some stupid mistake'. its frustrating because these are the same
people who will really understand the value of open source systems when
they see it. but you throw them off. maybe first few times they dont
understand. if you are so damn confident of gnu and its greatness then
eventually it WILL appeal to their senses that indeed gnu is the system
with lk as the core.

i think you will be absolutely surprised by the results. it will be `the
nice guy on the list helped me`....mentality is people will hear MORE of
what you have to say than less. thats Manners 101 for you.

technical life is not social life. please draw the difference between
flaming on technical issues rather than personal ones.

do what you do well. if you are a preacher then preach nicely.

frankly i started out much much more radical than you did [ask prabhu]
however i dont believe in it now, fundamentally dont believe in this kind
of zealotry, i would take the suits thank you . doing EE after CS has
helped me open up in that sense. i can sense frustration of a person who
cannot get a simple thing done and ask a small qn only to get immediately
flamed at the same being wholly competent in another field. its one word -
unprofessional.

if you want to be in mainstrame please grow up. otherwise you are always
indie, fringe, hippie whatever. go and cry on slashdot with the other
trolls.

i postponed this reply many times. now that ravi [hi:)] has spoken and
prof.sriram i decide to bite, because i am not interested in an individual
flamewar but vox populi.

thanks. regards,

			Vikram

hi
    .ps is PostScript file which can only be viewed in a PostScript viewer

here is a version of ghostview for windows
http://www.cs.wisc.edu/~ghost/gsview/index.htm
 download them

* sathish <sathish@mail.roc.co.in> [2002-12-11 10:29:36+0530]:

Satish> which is the best email client till now.

	You might want to start looking at pine, or mutt, if you feel brave
enough. There are some graphical mail readers too, such as Sylpheed, and VM
from inside XEmacs, which are quite nice, and powerful. Kmail sends out
lousy email, so I wouldn't suggest it, though I have no idea if the
interface is any good. It probably is considering so many people use it.

Satish> windows 2000 professional with outlook express. i lost all my 
Satish> reports and all important mails are gone.

	Dont you still have the folder with a bunch of dbx and pbx and
whatever files lying around? If yes, you can still run dbx => mbox convertor
programs and then view them with your favorite mail client.

	i.e. If outlook <whatever> cannot render your emails, thats OK. You
can still try and get back your stuff. If however your entire hard disk
died, tough luck.

	I have a cronjob that emails several different machines/hard disks
tarballs of my weekly emails ...

  Easy. In X-Window Open a Xterm Terminal OR

  In the command prompt type: gv mksfile.ps

  By using gv, U can view PDF files also.

I've seen many a flame and have myself posted saying let us avoid flaming.
I've seen such posts many a time from a few trying to correct everyone else
on Linux or GNU/Linux etc. While I like opensource and mean it in spirit, it
is quite irritating when some one keeps plugging in/nitpicking on semantics.
It is no different from flaming.

Dalda is a brand but became a generic name for cooking grease. History has
its ways. Similarly, Linux is recognised and understood by many and the
world at large as an opensource platform on which applications are
available. If I'm committing a technical blunder or spreading a lie for sake
of easy understanding, so be it. Just let others be. It does not make them
lesser mortals.

Mohan

GNU.  Calling the system Linux is false, it is the GNU system.

Hi,
If u want to find the contents of that package ..here is the command to do that:
$ rpm -ql  <package_name>
This basically queris for that package and gets the files in that.

For more see ,just rpm <return>
this will show the options in that.
Thanks
Giridharan

Subject: [Ilugc] RH 8.0 - Ideal Partitioning?
In-Reply-To: <1039597148.3df6fe5c3a028@webmail1.maa.sify.net>
References: <20021204114012.48649.qmail@web40602.mail.yahoo.com> <200212041243.SAA30403@hd2.dot.net.in> <1039597148.3df6fe5c3a028@webmail1.maa.sify.net>

Hi,

mea_culpa@sify.com wrote:
> Hi all,
> Am planning to install RH 8.0 (thanks to prof sriram :) ), have 5.5 GB
> of hard disk space, 128 MB RAM.
> Which is the ideal partioning and how much space should i allocate for
> each partition. The comp is going to be used for general home use --
> surfing the web, some openoffice applications, music and hopefully
> some games...

Everybody likes to do this differently, and it also depends on what
packages you plan to install. Anyway, my notebook has similar
constraints and here is how it is setup -

Part.   Size    Used
/       200MB   22MB
/var    300MB   79MB
/usr    2GB    920MB
/home   2GB    1.5GB
swap    260MB
/tmp    sym linked to /var/tmp/tmp

Btw I run debian. I don't run gnome/kde/games/openoffice, if you want
to use any of these you should consider making /usr larger.

Since I suspend this machine to disk it needs the extra swap space
(equal to RAM size). You may want to setup swap according to your
machine usage.

Some useful docs to read -

[1] The Multiple-Disk Howto http://www.tldp.org/HOWTO/Multi-Disk-HOWTO.html

[2] FreeBSD tuning(7) manpage (you will have to skip the BSD specific bits)
http://www.freebsd.org/cgi/man.cgi?query=tuning&manpath=FreeBSD+4.7-RELEASE

- Raja

From rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au  Wed Dec 11 11:20:35 2002
From: rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au (Raja Subramanian)
Date: Wed, 11 Dec 2002 22:20:35 +1100
Subject: [Ilugc] Printing in DOSEMU via telnet
In-Reply-To: <F155SFidMQPsq6DYq6f0000e8df@hotmail.com>
References: <F155SFidMQPsq6DYq6f0000e8df@hotmail.com>
Message-ID: <20021211112033.GC3539@pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au>

Hi,

krishna kumar wrote:
> We`re running Dosemu 1.0.1-2, and I`m having trouble with printing
> with a specific tailor-made application that we have here.  I`m
> trying to get it so that I can have a remote office connect to the
> system and print to their local printer.  Printing from that
> application doesn`t work unless a printer is directly attached to
> the computer. Is there any way around this, or any options or
> something that I could use..  I`ve been looking for information,
> and I hope that someone can help me here.  Thanks, kk.

The dosemu-HOWTO (included in the dosemu package describes) how to do
this.

Instead of redirecting LPT? to a device file like /dev/lp0, you can
redirect LPT? to an external program such as lpr/lp. The unix printing
system can then be setup for remote printing.

First, ensure that you can print to the remote printer using the unix
printing tools.

Once this is done, you need to change the relevent sections of your
dosemu.conf so that it looks something like this -

$_printer = "lp"    # list of (/etc/printcap) printer names to appear as
                    # LPT1, LPT2, LPT3 (not all are needed, empty for none)
$_printer_timeout = (20)# idle time in seconds before spooling out

$_ports = ""        # list of portnumbers such as "0x1ce 0x1cf 0x238"
                    # or "0x1ce range 0x280,0x29f 310"
                    # or "range 0x1a0,(0x1a0+15)"

In this example, the printer named "lp" is mapped to LPT1. You can also
assign different printers to the LPT1, LPT2 and LPT3 ports at the same
time.

- Raja

PS: Please post to this list in plain text (don't use html).

"Prakash N" wrote:

[snip]
>Its giving "undefined reference to pthread_create"

Its a linker error. not a compile error.
add "-lpthread" to the gcc commandline. It will link
in the pthread library. You may also need to add a 
-D_REENTRANT to ensure thread-safe library code.

cheers,
-Krish

Hello,

My name is Henrik Nilsen Omma, and I am one of the project leaders of a new 
Open Source Project called TheOpenCD.  Our aim is to create a simple to use CD 
distribution of Open Source software for Windows, and in that way spread the 
OSS message. I'm writing to various LUGs to announce the launch of our first 
edition, and hope that you might find it a useful tool in promoting Linux and 
OSS to a wider public.

The disc allows new users can try out Open Source software (OSS) in the  comfort
of their own, familiar operating system, rather than having to take  the drastic
step of reformatting their hard drive to install Linux or BSD. The  collection,
which includes OpenOffice.org, AbiWord and Beonex is primarily  intended for
non-technical computer users. However, we expect that the disc  will appeal
first to experienced OSS users, who will hopefully find it a  useful vehicle by
which to introduce OSS to their less computer-savvy friends.

We invite all OSS enthusiasts to download the ISO, burn CDs and distribute  them
widely to friends, local schools, universities, and companies.  We  further
encourage you all to stop by our to comment, discuss and contribute!

In /etc/passwd, you can chroot a user to his home directory as jailed /.
I think it is /<home> /  in the home directory entry. However, then, you
will need to symlink bin, sbin etc so that utilities work else no
command would work with the changed root. Quite a pain to set up one
like this I think. Any ideas from any one else?
 
Mohan

From sriram at aero.iitm.ernet.in  Thu Dec 12 06:44:02 2002
From: sriram at aero.iitm.ernet.in (P. Sriram)
Date: Thu, 12 Dec 2002 12:14:02 +0530 (IST)
Subject: [Ilugc] How to remove old kernels
In-Reply-To: <20021211232250.30042.qmail@web13709.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0212121205230.9042-100000@gateway.aero.iitm.ernet.in>

On Wed, 11 Dec 2002, Tamil Nadu wrote:

> I have installed new kernels as a patch through RedHat update, whenever
> my system boots up it display's all the old kernels. Is it possible to
> remove the old kernels, if so how. Will it affect other areas if i
> removed the old kernels. (Next kernel update i tried with "i" buy even
> then it display's the old kernel. Your help will be greatly appreciated.

hi,

i suppose you are updating using redhats up2date feature. i would not
quite call it a patch since it actually installs replacement packages and
deletes exisiting ones - except for kernel. if you delete an existing
(working) kernel and install a new one which does not boot, you are really
in bad shape since you machine is not bootable anymore. hence, it is
recommended to install new kernels using the i option (which leaves
existing kernel intact) rather than the u or f options (which delete old
packages and leave only the new version of package installed).  once you
check that the machine is booting, you could do a rpm -e (package name) to
erase the old version of the package. in your case, you could do an rpq -q
kernel to get a list of the installed kernel versions and then do rpm -e
kernelxxxx for each of the old kernel versions installed (xxx as printed
out by the rpm -q command). on the next boot, you will see only you latest 
kernel in the boot menu.

sriram

ps: all this can be found at our local redhat updates mirror site readme

From ganesan at boscoinfotech.com  Thu Dec 12 06:53:13 2002

Date: Thu, 12 Dec 2002 12:23:13 +0530 (IST)
Subject: [Ilugc] Printing in DOSEMU via telnet
In-Reply-To: <20021211112033.GC3539@pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au>
References: <F155SFidMQPsq6DYq6f0000e8df@hotmail.com>

If the remote client is DOS based, local printing can be done by inserting
an escape sequence to the text displayed.(ie) If you need it on the
printer at the client side.

The exact escape sequence depends on the type of 'term' you emulate.

-ASGanesan.

> krishna kumar wrote:
>> We`re running Dosemu 1.0.1-2, and I`m having trouble with printing
>> with a specific tailor-made application that we have here.  I`m
>> trying to get it so that I can have a remote office connect to the
>> system and print to their local printer.  Printing from that
>> application doesn`t work unless a printer is directly attached to the
>> computer. Is there any way around this, or any options or
>> something that I could use..  I`ve been looking for information, and I
>> hope that someone can help me here.  Thanks, kk.
>
> The dosemu-HOWTO (included in the dosemu package describes) how to do
> this.
>
> Instead of redirecting LPT? to a device file like /dev/lp0, you can
> redirect LPT? to an external program such as lpr/lp. The unix printing
> system can then be setup for remote printing.
>
> First, ensure that you can print to the remote printer using the unix
> printing tools.
>
> Once this is done, you need to change the relevent sections of your
> dosemu.conf so that it looks something like this -
>
> $_printer = "lp"    # list of (/etc/printcap) printer names to appear as
>                     # LPT1, LPT2, LPT3 (not all are needed, empty for
> none)
> $_printer_timeout = (20)# idle time in seconds before spooling out
>
> $_ports = ""        # list of portnumbers such as "0x1ce 0x1cf 0x238"
>                     # or "0x1ce range 0x280,0x29f 310"
>                     # or "range 0x1a0,(0x1a0+15)"
>
> In this example, the printer named "lp" is mapped to LPT1. You can also
> assign different printers to the LPT1, LPT2 and LPT3 ports at the same
> time.
>
> - Raja
>

On Thu, 2002-12-12 at 12:02, Bharathi S wrote:

>   If Ur using LILO BootLoader then edit the /etc/lilo.conf

If you are new to grub and have been on lilo for a while, you will be
amazed at the capabilities of grub. You donot have to run "grub" or
"grub-install" everytime after you update your menu.lst file (the
equivalent of lilo.conf). grub reads from the menu.lst file everytime
before it loads and uses information from it. grub can be like a mini
OS! it can read many filesystems like ext2, reiserfs, etc.,. Many a
times I tend to forget my root partition and grub comes into the play...
at the grub menu I just have to do:

grub> find /etc/fstab
(hd0,5)
(hd1,3)

grub> 

now from here, I can even look at the contents of the fstab file:

grub> root (hd0,5)
root (hd0,5)
filesystem type is ext2fs, partition type 0x83
grub> cat /etc/fstab
...
...
(contents of fstab file)
...
...
grub>


now I have a doubt, will grub continue to work if I remove menu.lst;
defragment my /boot filesystem; create menu.lst and without running
grub-install reboot the machine? there are things that I dont want to
try ;) has anybody tried this?

From sriram at aero.iitm.ernet.in  Thu Dec 12 07:44:29 2002
From: sriram at aero.iitm.ernet.in (P. Sriram)
Date: Thu, 12 Dec 2002 13:14:29 +0530 (IST)
Subject: [Ilugc] how to chkroot a user to their home directory
In-Reply-To: <61091.203.200.72.92.1039674678.squirrel@boscoinfotech.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0212121253070.10293-100000@gateway.aero.iitm.ernet.in>

On Thu, 12 Dec 2002, Subbarayan Ganesan wrote:
> In global login script check for the environement variable SSH_TTY and
> specific groups for which you want to chkroot. If true issue appropriate
> command.
[in reply to the original query]
> > Can any one help me in knowing how to chkroot a user to their home
> > directory for SSH access. Thanks for your help
> > Tamilnadulinks team http://www.tamilnadulinks.com

i thought it was chroot, not chkroot; anyway, chrooting a user to their 
home directory can have very bad effects. as pointed out by an earlier 
reply, this chroot will take /sbin, /bin and such things out of reach. 
symbolic links in the users' directory will not solve the problem - in 
fact, it will probably create circular symbolic links which lead nowhere. 
even things like bash will be out of reach. if you really want to do this, 
here is the way to do it.

(1) prepare a list of commands/programs/packages that the user is going to 
be allowed to use (including shells like bash)

(2) place a copy of every one of the items from (1) within the users' home 
directory; hard links or symbolic links will not work and the binaries 
will have to be here.

does not sound too bad, but actually, the worst is yet to come. every one 
of the programs copied to the users' directory in step (2) must be self 
contained. for statically linked packages, this is not a problem. however, 
most things will use dynamically linked libraries. in that case, there are 
two (both painful) options. we can recompile each of the chosen packages 
from (1) with statically linked libraries - which will bloat the packages 
like anything. the second option is to use ldd or some such tool to get a 
list of all the dynamic libraries used by all the packages and copy all 
these packages to the users' home directory (with the proper structure 
like /lib, /usr/lib etc under the home directory).

in short, it is probably not worth the effort. if the intent is to 
restrict what the user can do, there are other alternate approaches like 
restricted shells.

sriram




From sriram at aero.iitm.ernet.in  Thu Dec 12 08:12:35 2002
From: sriram at aero.iitm.ernet.in (P. Sriram)
Date: Thu, 12 Dec 2002 13:42:35 +0530 (IST)
Subject: [Ilugc] How to remove old kernels
In-Reply-To: <1039677690.23302.40.camel@suraj.cybernetsoft.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0212121319030.10886-100000@gateway.aero.iitm.ernet.in>

On 12 Dec 2002, Suraj Kumar wrote:
> now I have a doubt, will grub continue to work if I remove menu.lst;
> defragment my /boot filesystem; create menu.lst and without running
> grub-install reboot the machine? there are things that I dont want to
> try ;) has anybody tried this?

well, i have (unintentionally) tried a few of these, so i can reply. grub
will work if you remove menu.lst, but since there is no menu.lst, you will
straightaway get the grub> prompt. since no menu.lst file was read, there
will be no entries for kernel, root device etc. but, you can boot the
system from here by entering all the required stuff (kernel, root device).
defragging the /boot filesystem has no effect at all. at the time of
grub-install, the /boot partition entry (hdx,y) information is stored. as
long as this is not changed, grub will look at the /boot partition,(load
the stage 1 from the boot sector of that partition), see the file system
there and read all the appropriate files, from inside that file system -
including menu.lst (or grub.conf), kernel etc. (actually, i could be wrong
about the above since i have not tried it; the stage 1.5 might not load, i
suspect). however, if /boot does not exist as a separate partition but is
part of /, defragging this partition will probably screw things beyond
redemption (have not tried this; have no machines without separate /boot
partition). but seeing how good the functionality of grub is, i would not
be surprised if grub is able to work around this too (by seeing the /
partition and looking for the /boot directory inside that; it anyway looks
for the grub directory inside /boot, so it should not be too hard to look
for /boot inside / first and then doing the rest).

sriram

I'm not sure about what you want. 

Three distinct pieces of code:
1) The chat application itself (ie, the GUI)
2) Networking code 
3) The server 

(Chat client code) > (networking code) > (Chat server)

I assume that you are interested in the second layer (networking code).

Some questions:
+ Is your net-code application specific (just for your application)
+ Do you want a generic firewall (with a proxy capability)

On Wednesday 11 December 2002 14:09, you wrote:
> How to open .rpm files..

I read this tip somewhere. You do not need to be
root to install an rpm file. `open' the .rpm file (if that
is what you mean) in mc by hitting enter on its name.
It shows the directories and files in the package. One can
even copy the files to a temporary location and use them
(is possible)

If the rpm file is called foo-1.1.rpm
to list the files of a package rpm
      rpm -ql foo
to get the information on a package
     rpm -qi foo

From suraj at symonds.net  Fri Dec 13 04:07:53 2002
From: suraj at symonds.net (Suraj Kumar)
Date: Fri, 13 Dec 2002 09:37:53 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] editing in tamil
In-Reply-To: <200212121558.VAA08504@WS0005.indiatimes.com>
References: <200212121558.VAA08504@WS0005.indiatimes.com>

v_krishnakumar77 wrote on Thu, Dec 12, 2002 at 09:36:40PM +0530: 
,----
| Is there a HOWTO or a similar doc. for editing text in tamil ?
| 
| I have  the yudit editor  but have  no clues on  how to write  text in
| tamil.
| 
| This    screenshot   has    the    user   interface    in   tamil    !
| http://yudit.org/images/yudit-2.7.gif
`----

There is  Akaram TAB/TSC editor.   It also has a  nice Transliteration
keyboard using which you can  easily type tamil without having to know
the tamil  keyboard layout.  You can  download Akaram and  a few fonts
required for the same from:

		    ftp://ftp.tamillinux.org/apps/

Unfortunately  there is  no  such widely  adopted  standard for  tamil
typing. So  if you are planning  to write an article,  to say Kumudam,
you have to first  write a mail in english and ask  them what is their
Tamil Encoding Standard  and then send your document  in that standard
and send it across. Most do accept TSCII.

There  is a  mailing list  called tamilinix  (Note, not  tamillinux or
somesuch). This  is about tamil  computing on _any_ Unix  platform and
this isn't   necessarily  a free   software discussion list.   If  you
are a free software enthusiast, you can wear your anti-non-free filter
glasses and read their mailing list. because thats what I do...

	       http://groups.yahoo.com/group/tamilinix

HTH,

  -Suraj

Hi,

krishna kumar wrote:
> Thanks for the reply for the subject "Using Mailertable in sendmail".
> Is there any howto, article on configuring Split Horizon DNS.
> Thanks kk

I gather that you want to have two DNS "zones" -
	1. Public zone which is world visible, and a
	2. Private zone which is visible only inside your own network.

http://www.freebsddiary.org/privatedns.php will get you there in no
time. I've replicated this on our debian boxes running bind8 with great
success.

This document explains how to setup a single dns server to serve a
private and a public network with the correct restrictions on queries,
zone transfers, etc.

- Raja

PS: This is my last reply to any more of your html posts :(

<html><div style='background-color:'><DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>
<DIV>My knowledge about split-horizon dns is that it's not two DNS servers, it just means that your DNS server gives <BR>different ips for the same names to queries from internal vs external. <BR>Added to that with ISC's BIND, one can create a "stub" "zone" for each domain, listing the IP address of the replacement content DNS server in "named.conf" and reconfiguring the content DNS server to support the "zone transfer" DNS database replication mechanism. </DIV>
<DIV>Is there any webpage containing the practical example or instructions on how to setup split horizon using bind9. </DIV>
<DIV>Thanks,<BR>kk</DIV>
<DIV>p.s. Setting up of split-horizon was suggested by Mr. Balasubramaniam, based on my query, which goes as, <BR>sending emails to the internal domain (clients) without isp dns lookup (as we are connecting to the external world through dialup). Hope this info. would help others too. </DIV></div><br clear=all><hr>Protect your PC - <a href="http://g.msn.com/8HMJEN/2024">Click here</a> for McAfee.com VirusScan Online </html>

From sriram at aero.iitm.ernet.in  Fri Dec 13 08:01:47 2002
From: sriram at aero.iitm.ernet.in (P. Sriram)
Date: Fri, 13 Dec 2002 13:31:47 +0530 (IST)
Subject: [Ilugc] GRUB in 7.3
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0212122311500.6440-100000@mrna.tn.nic.in>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0212131316230.32012-100000@gateway.aero.iitm.ernet.in>

On Thu, 12 Dec 2002 km@mrna.tn.nic.in wrote:
> while i loaded RHL 7.3 it asked for a grub password which i supplied.
> but after installation when i booted the system,  it doesnt ask for the
> GRUB password at all-- why ?
> kindly enlighten me of  having a password like that ?

hi,

the password as above is meant to prevent access to non-standard booting
(for example, booting into single user mode; prevents interactive access
to grub, actually*). standard booting will proceed without the password.  
if you want to protect a particular boot image with a password, you will
have to edit the /etc/grub.conf file and put a lock or password statement
inside the appropriate image section. the password statement is more
flexible since it allows a per-image password while the lock statement
will ask for the common password. read the info page of grub (the section
on security) to get more details.

sriram

*: it may sound inocuous, but interactive access to grub is very 
dangerous. forget entering the system in single user mode; you can do 
more. since grub understands file systems, but does not implement file 
ownership and access controls, there are many many things you can do from 
the grub command line. you could cat /etc/shadow, for example (if you know 
which disk partition is holding /etc/); and, since the system has not 
booted yet, you will leave no trace in any log files....

From tamilnadulinks at yahoo.com  Fri Dec 13 13:49:11 2002
From: tamilnadulinks at yahoo.com (Tamil Nadu)
Date: Fri, 13 Dec 2002 05:49:11 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [Ilugc] reg adding swap partition.
In-Reply-To: <5.2.0.9.0.20021213183620.01424c30@mail.roc.co.in>
Message-ID: <20021213134911.42564.qmail@web13704.mail.yahoo.com>

--0-291210279-1039787351=:40908
Content-Type: text/plain; charset=us-ascii


You have to add swap only if you have increased your RAM, increasing the size of the hard disk partition doesn't require you to increase the swap size. If you have increased the RAM this is the process for increasing the swap file size. 
Linux can happily accept more than one swap partitions. Infact,             
it doesn't need to be a partition. It only needs to be a file with 
continuous 
storage. (This is explained in man mkswap)

So you can create a file like this:
dd if=/dev/zero of=/usr/extraswap bs=1024 count=65536
# to create 64 MB swap (I think there's a limit of 128MB for each file)

Swap file needs a signature before you can use it:
mkswap /usr/extraswap

#Start using the swap
swapon /usr/extraswap

#See it in action
top

You can also put it in /etc/fstab so that it is picked automatically
after each boot (by swapon -a from rc scripts)


Also read the lines below for your reference

Actually it is an erroneous recommendation for most people. For kernels
2.4.0 - 2.4.9, There was a quite radical VM (Virtual Memory) system 
that
provided great performance, at the cost of some predictability (Rik Van
Riel wrote it, you can search for that name on google.com/linux and
probably get more info about it). One of the things that helped the
system function more effectively was to have 2xRAM as your swap. The
reasons for this are complex and I don't fully understand them.

What I do know is that the VM that was plugged in for 2.4.10 and later,
which brought more stability, has no such recommendation. I generally
make swap equal to RAM upon system install, but I don't fret over it
after that. On a workstation, if you're swapping a lot, you might want
more, but performance is only going to suffer. On a server, swapping is
probably out of line, and should be dealt with by popping in some more
RAM.

If you think RAM is too expensive... think again. 


I used to run my DNS, web, and mail server, on an AMD 5x86-133. This is
essentially a really fast 486. When I first installed the system, it 
had
24MB of 486 Parity RAM. I added some php and 5 email users to the
system, and things started getting ugly. Mainly because I had to switch
from using boa, to apache. I had 128MB of swap space, and about 40% of
that was in use at all times. I went online, bought 128MB of EDO RAM,
and threw it in there. Suddenly everything happened in memory, and I 
was
able to host my website, getting 250 - 1000 hits a day, and eventually
about 15 email users' accounts off that server. Only after I added 5
more websites, all using php, did I have to upgrade it.

My point is, RAM is cheap, and sometimes offers more of a performance
gain than CPU or even faster hard disks. Treat your box to some today!
;-)


Regards

Tamilnadulinks team http://www.tamilnadulinks.com

> You have to add swap only if you have increased your RAM, increasing the size of the hard disk partition doesn't require you to increase the swap size. If you have increased the RAM this is the process for increasing the swap file size. 

This is nonsensical. If I can't add more RAM, then the only other way is
to increase my swap. Ofcourse, I wouldn't be too happy with the
performance on Linux.

> Linux can happily accept more than one swap partitions. Infact,             

<snip>

> Also read the lines below for your reference
> 
> Actually it is an erroneous recommendation for most people. For kernels
> 2.4.0 - 2.4.9, There was a quite radical VM (Virtual Memory) system 
> that
> provided great performance, at the cost of some predictability (Rik Van
> Riel wrote it, you can search for that name on google.com/linux and
> probably get more info about it). One of the things that helped the
> system function more effectively was to have 2xRAM as your swap. The
> reasons for this are complex and I don't fully understand them.

One of the problems that I can see here, is that vendors DO NOT ship
vanilla kernels (Debian being the exception). For example, Redhat in its
8 "dot oh" version seems to have put in some realtime kernel code, which
is not officially part of 2.4 series. uname will still report 2.4.x, but
its not vanilla.

Personally, I don't care for fine-grained performance hacks. But, thats
just me. 

> What I do know is that the VM that was plugged in for 2.4.10 and later,
> which brought more stability, has no such recommendation. I generally
> make swap equal to RAM upon system install, but I don't fret over it
> after that. On a workstation, if you're swapping a lot, you might want
> more, but performance is only going to suffer. On a server, swapping is
> probably out of line, and should be dealt with by popping in some more
> RAM.

I would definitely choose to fall back on swap with a performance hit,
than totally kill my application. 

> If you think RAM is too expensive... think again. 

I have been trying again and again to "think", but the price of 3200 is
not dropping. Nor is Crucial/Kingston/Samsung announcing a price slash.
:(

> I used to run my DNS, web, and mail server, on an AMD 5x86-133. This is
<snip stuff irrelevant to topic>

> provided great performance, at the cost of some predictability (Rik Van
> Riel wrote it, you can search for that name on google.com/linux and
> probably get more info about it). One of the things that helped the
> system function more effectively was to have 2xRAM as your swap. The
> reasons for this are complex and I don't fully understand them.

One of the problems that I can see here, is that vendors DO NOT ship
vanilla kernels (Debian being the exception). For example, Redhat in its
8 "dot oh" version seems to have put in some realtime kernel code, which
is not officially part of 2.4 series. uname will still report 2.4.x, but
its not vanilla.

Personally, I don't care for fine-grained performance hacks. But, thats
just me. 

> What I do know is that the VM that was plugged in for 2.4.10 and later,
> which brought more stability, has no such recommendation. I generally
> make swap equal to RAM upon system install, but I don't fret over it
> after that. On a workstation, if you're swapping a lot, you might want
> more, but performance is only going to suffer. On a server, swapping is
> probably out of line, and should be dealt with by popping in some more
> RAM.

I would definitely choose to fall back on swap with a performance hit,
than totally kill my application. 

> If you think RAM is too expensive... think again. 

I have been trying again and again to "think", but the price of 3200 is
not dropping. Nor is Crucial/Kingston/Samsung announcing a price slash.
:(

> I used to run my DNS, web, and mail server, on an AMD 5x86-133. This is



Ganesh
PS: I would appreciate it if you could use your name. Anonymous mails
are just weird. And, yes, I know your name is Raja.

> Regards
> 
> Tamilnadulinks team http://www.tamilnadulinks.com

Subject: [Ilugc] how to install tamil fonts in linux
In-Reply-To: <20021213235825.38886.qmail@web13705.mail.yahoo.com>

On Fri, 13 Dec 2002, Tamil Nadu wrote:

> Is there is a way to install tamil fonts in Linux

In RH 8:
  Download the font frm the website and put it in .fonts
  dir in ur home dir.

In lesser versions
  Copy it in /usr/share/fonts/truetype/ Dir. And U need
  XFSTT Server to render the TTF fonts.

From v_krishnakumar77"<v_krishnakumar77 at indiatimes.com  Sat Dec 14 10:13:53 2002
From: v_krishnakumar77"<v_krishnakumar77 at indiatimes.com (v_krishnakumar77)
Date: Sat, 14 Dec 2002 15:43:53 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] how to install tamil fonts in linux
Message-ID: <200212141005.PAA06747@WS0005.indiatimes.com>


"Bharathi S"<bharathi@lantana.TeNeT.res.in> wrote:
On Fri, 13 Dec 2002, Tamil Nadu wrote:

> Is there is a way to install tamil fonts in Linux
[snip]

>In lesser versions
>  Copy it in /usr/share/fonts/truetype/ Dir. And U >need
>  XFSTT Server to render the TTF fonts.
Recent versions of XFree86 (starting from 4.x ?) directly use the FreeType module to render ttf/t1 fonts. So a font server is not required. 

IMO, to install fonts this is preferable:

1. copy the fonts to a seperate dir 
2. run "ttmkfdir -o fonts.scale" in the dir
3. add a "FontPath path_to_ur_fonts" entry in the X configuration file.

This way, if a buggy font causes u trouble (I recently got bit by a few buggy chess fonts!) u can simply remove the font path and everything will work fine.


HTH,
-Krish

Apart from this, if you add the fonts in your home directory in the folder
.fonts
it will automatically render those fonts into the applications. This is
possible in RH8.0

From suraj at symonds.net  Sun Dec 15 04:02:46 2002
From: suraj at symonds.net (Suraj Kumar)
Date: Sun, 15 Dec 2002 09:32:46 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] making bootable cds
In-Reply-To: <200212150837.45270.mohanakrishnan@softhome.net>
References: <200212150837.45270.mohanakrishnan@softhome.net>
Message-ID: <20021215040246.GA730@suraj.sytes.net>

Mohanakrishnan wrote on Sun, Dec 15, 2002 at 08:37:45AM +0530: 

,----
| 	can someone  brief on how to  make bootable cds...  i have the
| iso's of the debian woody cds on  my hdd, i wud like to burn them onto
| cds and tried burning the  first of the six using gnome-toaster... but
| looks like the cd hasn't been made bootable...
`----

If you  want a  luser-friendly alternative (I  heard this one  is like
nero), you can  try kreateCD (its a debian package  in stable. i think
its not there in the testing CDs  that I gave you). You may first have
to use the woody ISOs to install KreateCD. You can do this as follows:

1. mount the ISOs over loop

for i in $(seq 1 7)
do   
  mount -o ro,loop -t iso9660 /wherever/woody/woody$i.iso /mnt/woody/$i
done

2. Add entries to /etc/apt/sources.list for using these ISOs:

for i in $(seq 1 7)
do
 echo "deb file:/mnt/woody/$i woody main contrib" >>/etc/apt/sources.list
 echo "deb file:/mnt/woody/$i woody/non-US main contrib" >>/etc/apt/sources.list
done

3. tell apt about you changes: goto dselect; select 'update'

4. install kreateCD:

apt-get install kreatecd

have fun!

   -Suraj

>can someone  brief on how to  make bootable cds...  >i have the iso's of the debian woody cds on  my hdd, >i wud like to burn them onto

Hmm... strange! Did u try cdrecord ?

I have used cdrecord to write boot CDs for Solaris 8, FreeBSD, Mandrake 8 etc and never had any problems.

If the ISO image is built with the el-torito flag then all u need to do is just burn the image. So if its a stock ISO image, then u should'nt have any problems. If u built the image, then checkout the man page for mkisofs (especially lookout for "-b")

From manoaj at kotak.net  Sun Dec 15 06:52:37 2002
From: manoaj at kotak.net (Dosai)
Date: Sun, 15 Dec 2002 12:22:37 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] (no subject)

Minutes of Ilugc meet 14th DEC 2002 (Sat)

As per the tradition of ilugc the meet started off late at around 3.30 pm.
There were a few people present.
The speaker who agreed to talk on Intrusion Detection (Mr Amresh) was not
there so we were in search of ideas to start the meet and to keep it going .

1) Our LUG coordinator - Mr Bharathi took the stage first and gave us all an
intro about how BangLinux was conducted. The entry to banglinux was 300/-
which included a T-shirt, lunch for 3 days and coffee. He said that there
were people selling linux distros and proggies.

SOmu distributed some T-shirts meanwhile :)

2) Somu came to the dias after this to deliver a talk on SSH, Basic features
of SSH and what ssh can do. The talk started with somu giving us an intro to
Public key, private key, session key , type of encryption used and
pass-phrases (secure way of using ssh).

        Then somu proceeded to talk on ssh-agents which are used to automate
processes which are tiring like remembering many pass-phrases. He talked
about how to go about adding public keys of various boxes to the ssh agent
using the ssh - add command.

        Then he talked about how to make other services use ssh using port
forwarding. He explained this using a scenario.
                Consider two boxes (one local and one remote). The remote
box has an imap server running on it and the local box wants to access the
imap server to read mails using the secuity of SSH. To attain this the ssh
tunnel is exablished between the server and the client and the imap port
number is binded to another free port on which the ssh listens.This is done
using the command

                                    #ssh L:2001:143:R
where L = local, R=remote , 143 = imap port, 2001 = free port

Then there was a part on agent-forwarding. This is turned on using
forwardagent yes.

Then there was again a case in which there are 2 boxes H (home) and W(work).
The box W is protected from the NET by another box B. When someone wants to
login into W, the person has to login through B to get to W. This can be
done by

1. ssh from H to B and
2 ssh from B to W.
But this case is impossible because the box B does not store any keys. So
agent forwarding comes into action. In this all the keys are stored in the
machine H itself.

BOTTOM LINE - The box B acts as a transperant layer between H and W. (there
were some questions from all sides on this one). Somu finished his talk with
this.

At this point the meet got over and veeryone moved out except a few of us
who were chit-chatting.Then the group of me,Suresh,Bharathi,somu went to
have some coffee in Nandhinee's where we met prabhu with a few of his
friends. There was a little conversation on flamewars there. With this the
meet ended.

Any corrections/ comments welcome :)


Regards
Dosai
