From sriram at aero.iitm.ernet.in  Sun Dec 15 11:28:04 2002
From: sriram at aero.iitm.ernet.in (P. Sriram)
Date: Sun, 15 Dec 2002 16:58:04 +0530 (IST)
Subject: [Ilugc] remote login
In-Reply-To: <200212150828.47862.mohanakrishnan@softhome.net>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0212151652290.11977-100000@gateway.aero.iitm.ernet.in>

On Sun, 15 Dec 2002, Mohanakrishnan wrote:
> 	i have about 10 old pentium-I machines, without harddisks, i want to 
> connect them to my network thru remote login... although i heard 
> ot remote login i hardly know anything about this... so pls 
> guide me on how i shud go about from the scratch... 

first, you will need to have some boot device on the machines - this could
be floppy or a boot rom on a network card. more importantly, you need to
decide first what kind of connectivity you want to provide from these
nodes. for example, you can put dos and telnet on a floppy and use these
as telnet terminals (sort of like dumb terminals). you could boot dos and
use these as vnc terminals with a vnc server (or servers) running
somewhere on your network - that will give you graphic terminals. at the
other extreme, you could build full diskless linux boxes out of these -
the user wont know it is a diskless machine. of course, with present linux
distributions, pentium machines will feel a bit slow. depending on which 
option you want, i can give a step by step solution.

sriram



From smohan at vsnl.com  Sun Dec 15 13:55:56 2002
From: smohan at vsnl.com (S Mohan)
Date: Sun, 15 Dec 2002 19:25:56 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] Chroot applications
Message-ID: <000001c2a441$b23fcb70$36405bca@18yamuna>

Addendum to an earlier mail on chrooting to while I had replied and so
had Prof Sriram. I do not know if this would relieve you of creating
symlinks to allow access to common utilities. Have not tried it myself.
Will do soon and let the group know. In the meanwhile, other could try
this too.

Chroot all apps you want
The script http://www.chronox.de/chroot/chroot-0.1.tar.bz2 can be used
to put any application in a chroot jail, removing any capabilities or
let it run under a different user ID. 
Tested with Squid, rinted, SSH, Portmapper. 

Updated to version 0.1 on August 24 2002 

It uses a helper program

hello,

harris ur rahman wanted us to know:

> hi all,
> 
> 	Prof sriram was sayin somthin bout Shadow. Faintly understand it 
> hath to do with passwords. Enlightenment please.

The idea is not to keep your passwords in /etc/passwd which is world
readable. Have another file /etc/shadow to keep your passwords which is
only readable by root.

Any basic book on UNIX will explain this. You could also type "shadow
passwords" in google for further funda. 


> 	I opened the file from fstab it contained an entry for the 
> usernames in my comp for linux fillowed by some numbers . How 
> important is it

Pardon me. fstab ?

> " [OFF - Topic] :there was a disscussion about images being 
> rectangular shaped. is it possible to have an irregular shaped 
> form in VB."

Yes, again google is your friend. I can't recall those obscure APIs off
my head. If you want me to search, email me offlist, but I'll take my
own sweet time.

On Sunday 15 December 2002 08:37, Mohanakrishnan wrote:
> can someone brief on how to make bootable cds... i have the iso's
> of the debian woody cds on my hdd, i wud like to burn them onto cds and
> tried burning the first of the six using gnome-toaster... but looks like
> the cd hasn't been made bootable...

I don't know what gnome-toaster does but the command
# cdrecord file.iso
with proper options writes an image to disk. The image
has to be bootable. mkisofs will say how to make an image
bootable. mkisofs is not needed when the image is available.

>         i checked out the howtos of cd writing, which doesn't have anything 
> to say on bootable cds. waiting for replies...
grep the CD-Writing-HOWTO for bootable, El Torito

From rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au  Mon Dec 16 03:17:14 2002
From: rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au (Raja Subramanian)
Date: Mon, 16 Dec 2002 14:17:14 +1100
Subject: [Ilugc] making bootable cds
In-Reply-To: <200212150837.45270.mohanakrishnan@softhome.net>
References: <200212150837.45270.mohanakrishnan@softhome.net>
Message-ID: <20021216031714.GA30583@pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au>

Hi,

Mohanakrishnan wrote:
> 	can someone brief on how to make bootable cds... i have the iso's of 
> the debian woody cds on my hdd, i wud like to burn them onto cds and 
> tried burning the first of the six using gnome-toaster... but looks 
> like the cd hasn't been made bootable...
> 

The debian iso's are already bootable. You just need to burn them
correctly. Here is how I do it (and it works on x86, sparc and ppc) -

cdrecord -fs=16M -v -eject speed=8 dev=0,6,0 -data -pad diskimg.iso

You will need to replace "speed", "dev", and "diskimg.iso" with your own
values. Ensure that the disk image has an "iso" extension.

The debian_on_cd faq has more (including cd writing using windows
software) -
	http://www.debian.org/CD/faq/#record-unix

- Raja

On Mon, 2002-12-16 at 14:34, barkkarn aravinda wrote:
> any one tell me the initialization string for the
> modem.my default initialization string is ATZ.

wvdialconf (a part of wvdial) will find out all the required
initialisation strings. General problem is when you want your modem to
_not_ wait for the dialtone. put ATX0 instead of ATQ in that case.

From AnoopS at virtusa.com  Mon Dec 16 13:17:22 2002
From: AnoopS at virtusa.com (Anoop Kumar Saxena)
Date: Mon, 16 Dec 2002 08:17:22 -0500
Subject: [Ilugc] C  my doubt
Message-ID: <CB8215AD270F3F4B82E6B04F567C0AC41A30E7@eipmailsvr.erunway.atc.dns>

Header files have an extension .h most of the times, and all the
declarations(prototypes) (should) go there. The actual code is in the
libraries which get linked dynamically.
www.google.comlookforstaticandsharedlibraries

you can also use "libc" to narrow down your search.

hi

>   * The header files contain just prototypes
>   Where does the actual code for performing an i/o , say using
> scanf() or printf() lie.  As far as i have seen the header files
> dont contain this code (correct me if i am wrong).

you are right !.header files contain only prototypes.
the  actual code for scanf/printf/any library function for that matter are
linked
to the file.they usually exist as library files , in linux they are in .o
(object files ), .a(library archive file)
  .so (shared object file).scanf/printf are in glibc.you can find their
implementation in
glibc's source code.

Manikandan P.

Hi,


>In case, I need to format my entire hard disk, how do I backup my mails?  
>Which is the folder (~/Mail, I suppose) I have to backup and how can I retrieve the same?

To backup:
tar jcf mail-backup.tar.bz2 ~/Mail

To restore:
cd 
tar jxvf  PATH_TO_BACKUP_FILE/mail-backup.tar.bz2


>to the same state of kmail after formating?
State should be restored.

Gurus, correct me if I'm wrong.

cheers,

From v_krishnakumar77"<v_krishnakumar77 at indiatimes.com  Tue Dec 17 10:36:33 2002
From: v_krishnakumar77"<v_krishnakumar77 at indiatimes.com (v_krishnakumar77)
Date: Tue, 17 Dec 2002 16:06:33 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] Doubts on Sockets
Message-ID: <200212171029.PAA32584@WS0005.indiatimes.com>


"Prakash N" wrote:


Hi All,


>I have a small doubt in Sockets..
Hmmm. Seems like its not a small doubt after all !


>We use sockets for sending data accross the processes.
If the processes are running on the same machine consider using shared memory - its much faster.

>I am using a TCP socket for such communication.


>I need to send one structure using Sockets.


>Now please let me know how can I write my structure into the buffer(one of the parameter of send System Call)

XDR (try googling for it) is a pretty good solution and its the underlying encoding scheme in RPC. 

CDR (google for the spec.) is a variant of XDR that is used in CORBA. 

Another scheme is to use XML to encode structures. This is very simple to use but carries a bit of baggage as it requires an XML parser. But it can be easily debugged. IMO, its the simplest way to encode data. 

For some testimonials, checkout http://www.xmlrpc.com

hth,
-Krish

From suraj at symonds.net  Wed Dec 18 04:05:06 2002
From: suraj at symonds.net (Suraj Kumar)
Date: Wed, 18 Dec 2002 09:35:06 +0530
Subject: [ilugc] wvdial.conf help
In-Reply-To: <20021217125442.18951.qmail@webmail29.rediffmail.com>
References: <20021217125442.18951.qmail@webmail29.rediffmail.com>
Message-ID: <20021218040506.GD1344@suraj.sytes.net>

A.Guru  prasadh wrote on Tue, Dec 17, 2002 at 12:54:42PM -0000: 
,----
| Init1=ATX0
| Init2=ATQ0 V1 E1 S0=0 &C1 &D2 S11=55 +FCLASS=0
`----

Your Init1 is ATX0 (that asks wvdial to not wait for the dialtone) and
Init2 has  ATQ0 (which asks wvdial  to _wait_ for  a dialtone).

From smohan at vsnl.com  Wed Dec 18 05:24:10 2002

My experience with Indian line conditions have been that wait for dial tone
option normally does not work half the time even though we can hear the dial
tone - something to do with the dial tone recognition being very stringent.
I use no wait for dial tone but sleep for 10 seconds using , in the number.
This works fine for me.

Mohan

on and on...). :(

I have been enjoying pseudo-overloading in C by using function pointers,
and passing references to structures.

hello,

slash_axl_rose_upen wanted us to know:

> hi all
> I want to learn mysql on linux but i have not worked
> with sql also
> how do i get started and which is a good book for sql
> on linux
> thnkx in advance

Please do not cross post.

Since you say you haven't worked with SQL before, it might be better to
get started with postgresql.

There are tons of information out there for you to get started. Make
sure you have a reference to Generic SQL, and not extensions like P/SQL.

There are also programs that "translate" your queries into SQL.

The best way to learn is by doing. You learn to code by _writing_ code,
and not by _reading_ books. Just like you learn to ride a bicycle by riding
it and not by reading how to ride. [1] 

	Ganesh

[1] I don't claim to be the first person to say that.

From sriram at aero.iitm.ernet.in  Wed Dec 18 08:01:02 2002
From: sriram at aero.iitm.ernet.in (P. Sriram)
Date: Wed, 18 Dec 2002 13:31:02 +0530 (IST)
Subject: [ilugc] wvdial.conf help
In-Reply-To: <20021218040506.GD1344@suraj.sytes.net>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0212181251240.26744-100000@gateway.aero.iitm.ernet.in>

On Wed, 18 Dec 2002, Suraj Kumar wrote:
> A.Guru  prasadh wrote on Tue, Dec 17, 2002 at 12:54:42PM -0000: 
> ,----
> | Init1=ATX0
> | Init2=ATQ0 V1 E1 S0=0 &C1 &D2 S11=55 +FCLASS=0
> `----
> Your Init1 is ATX0 (that asks wvdial to not wait for the dialtone) and
> Init2 has  ATQ0 (which asks wvdial  to _wait_ for  a dialtone). 

this is not quite correct. Q0 only turns on response mode so that the
modem returns results when it receives commands. the opposite setting is
Q1 which puts the modem in quiet mode (ie) the modem will not reply to any
commands sent but will quietly execute them (hopefully). X0 is not the
preferred setting for 'do not wait for dial tone'; actually, X0 puts the
modem in basic 300 baud modem response mode (yes, that is 300 baud, which
only oldies like me would have seen/used in real life). X1 or X3 are
usually the preferred settings for blind dialing. your modem documentation
(however limited that may be) may help. most modems will go into blind
dialing mode with X1 or X3.

sriram

>How can you overload a function in C?
1. Macros in conjunction with the ability to change the name of the
generated assembly symbol ?
2. a precompiler ?
3. use a C++ compiler ;-)


----------Will it then be called overloading? Overloading essentially will
have to involve late binding and so the 1st 2 options are ruled out. 3rd
option is ummmm wellllllllllllllllll not admissible :>)

If you are talking about dynamic dispatch, then there are 2 options I can think of:
1. A VMT approach as used in C++ and most other OO languages.
This approach is fast but it is quite cumbersome to add features like reflection etc.

2. A runtime messenger approach as used in Objective-C and CLOS. 
This approach although slightly slower offers tremendous flexibility. It is very easy to add features like reflection, runtime loading of classes, modifying methods at runtime, adding methods to existing classes etc. Another advantage of this approach is that you can also dispatch events with the runtime messenger. 

btw, have u looked at Objective-C ?

To build the kernel, u need fasm (fasm.sf.net).

From bga at vsnl.com  Wed Dec 18 11:08:23 2002
From: bga at vsnl.com (BGanesh)
Date: Wed, 18 Dec 2002 16:38:23 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] [info] postgresql in a production environment
Message-ID: <200212181108.QAA22317@hd2.dot.net.in>

Hello,

	Last week, we at ETV implemented a postgreSQL backend for election results 
updates at Gujarat. There were twelve input clients, and three output clients 
which generated realtime on air graphics. Clients were all Windows 2000 
(anybody know of any good character generators ala CG2000 from matrox running 
on Linux?). 

	There were two Linux machines running postgresql, in an almost failsafe 
environment. The secondary database would pull the most recent data every 
minute via a cron job from the primary and update itself. In case the primary 
db failed, it would shoot the primary (if it was still alive), and take over 
by a simple ip change (I know I know, there are better ways). The clients 
with uncommited transactions would rollback, and the data remains online with 
a worst case scenario of 30 seconds downtime. When the first machine came 
back online in such a scenario, it would begin functioning as the 
secondary... 

	What would make postgres production ready is realtime replication, and I 
guess that would be available in ver 7.3 (any ETA for this?).

	Downsides : The developers were from the Windows world, and made certain 
incorrect assumptions (ex, setup and teardown of tables is fast in MS 
sql2000, and quite slow in postgres; and since they were unaware of this fact 
they were creating temporary tables all over the place for complex queries). 
So, the only problem was their unfamiliarity with the tools....

	in a related note, is anybody aware of MS-Access like DB's for Linux (as in 
ease of use) ? 

regards
BGa

No you need worry not. This is general behaviour of
unix like systems. Once a programme exited, the RAM is
flushed only when there is shortage of memory for
something else. That's why you will see that,
generally programmes start quicker second time than
first time.

From suraj at symonds.net  Thu Dec 19 05:02:47 2002
From: suraj at symonds.net (Suraj Kumar)
Date: Thu, 19 Dec 2002 10:32:47 +0530
Subject: [long] Re: [Ilugc] Mail attachment in php
In-Reply-To: <3E0068F5.73222D86@locustechnologies.com>
References: <3E0068F5.73222D86@locustechnologies.com>
Message-ID: <20021219050247.GA4166@suraj.sytes.net>

S.Balasubramanian wrote on Wed, Dec 18, 2002 at 05:54:21PM +0530: 

,----
| How to send attachment through mail in php.  Please explain.
`----

A Mail attachment isn't a seperate entity in Internet mail.  The stock
mail functions in PHP donot have a way of adding attachments as simply
as  passing a filename  parameter!  (I've  heard JSP  has a  rich mail
class where you pass a filename as a parameter).

I'm  giving a  quick howto  on  sending an  attachment.  Before  doing
anything,  send  a mail  with  attachments  to  you@localhost and  cat
/var/spool/mail/you.   Try and  understand how  it is  formatted.  All
Internet  mails have  a  Content-Type header  and  a 'boundary'.   The
boundary specifies the start and end of each section within a mail.

The mail msg will use  the "randomstring" specified in the boundary to
differentiate between various parts of  your mail. For instance a mail
with a short message and a small attachment will be like this:

Mail header:

 Content-Type: <content type>; boundary="randomstring"

Mail Body:

 --randomstring
 Content-Type: text/plain; charset=us-ascii
 Content-Disposition: inline
 
 this is the mail's main message.  this is not an attachment. your MUA
 will display this.
 
 --randomstring
 Content-Type: text/plain; charset=us-ascii
 Content-Disposition: attachment; filename="attachment.txt"
 
 this is the content of the attachment.
 --randomstring--

 
Here,   the   various  portions   of   your   mail   starts  with   a
--<randomstring> and the entire  stuff ends with a --<randomstring>--
(note the trailing '--'s).

To sum up all this, the following PHP code should give a small idea of
how you can implement this:

<?

function random_string($len) {

	 srand((double) microtime() * 1000000);
	 for ($i = 0; $i < $len; $i++) {
	     $ret = $ret . chr (rand (65, 65 + 25));
	 }

	 return $ret;
}

function add_attachment(&$body, $boundary, $attachment_file) {
  
  static $init = false;
  
  $fp = fopen ($attachment_file, 'r');
  $file_data = fread ($fp, filesize ($attachment_file));
  $abs_filename = preg_replace ('/.*\//', '', $attachment_file);
  $buffer = "\r\n" . '--' . $boundary . "\r\n";
  
  $buffer = $buffer . 'Content-Type: text/plain; charset=us-ascii' . "\r\n";
  $buffer = $buffer . 'Content-Disposition: attachment; filename="' 
    . $abs_filename . '"' 
    . "\r\n\r\n";
  
  $buffer = $buffer . $file_data;
  
  if (!$init) {
    $pre = '--' . $boundary . "\r\n"
      . 'Content-Type: text/plain; charset=us-ascii' . "\r\n"
      . 'Content-Disposition: inline' . "\r\n\r\n";
    $init = true;
  }
  
  $body = $pre . $body . $buffer;
}

function end_attachments(&$body, $boundary) {
  $body = $body . "\r\n" . '--' . $boundary . '--' . "\r\n";
}

function get_header($boundary) {
  return 'Content-Type: multipart/mixed; boundary="' . $boundary . '"';
}

//main

$message = "hi,\nhow are you?\n";

$boundary = random_string(10);
add_attachment($message, $boundary, "/con/con/foo.txt");
add_attachment($message, $boundary, "/con/con/bar.txt");
end_attachments($message, $boundary);
$header = get_header($boundary);
$to = 'suraj@localhost';
$subject = 'attachment test';

mail ($to, $subject, $message, $header);

?>

I would recommend  you to find a full-blown  attachment class first at
phpclasses.org.  What I've given above is just a sample to demonstrate
how to do attachments in PHP.  For sending binary data you may have to
handle a lot more different techniques (base64 encoding, etc.,).  Read
the appropriate RFCs (rfc822, rfc1521,  rfc1522), if you plan to write
your  own ones.  (note that  most of  the code  at  phpclasses.org are
GPLed,  so  it is  illegal  to  misuse  them for  writing  proprietary
applications).
 
  -Suraj

> S.Balasubramanian wrote on Wed, Dec 18, 2002 at
> 05:54:21PM +0530: 
> 
> ,----
> | How to send attachment through mail in php. 
> Please explain.
> `----
> 
> A Mail attachment isn't a seperate entity in
> Internet mail.  The stock
> mail functions in PHP donot have a way of adding
> attachments as simply
> as  passing a filename  parameter!  (I've  heard JSP
>  has a  rich mail
> class where you pass a filename as a parameter).
> 
> I'm  giving a  quick howto  on  sending an 
> attachment.  Before  doing
> anything,  send  a mail  with  attachments  to 
> you@localhost and  cat
> /var/spool/mail/you.   Try and  understand how  it
> is  formatted.  All
> Internet  mails have  a  Content-Type header  and  a
> 'boundary'.   The
> boundary specifies the start and end of each section
> within a mail.
> 
> The mail msg will use  the "randomstring" specified
> in the boundary to
> differentiate between various parts of  your mail.
> For instance a mail
> with a short message and a small attachment will be
> like this:
> 
> Mail header:
> 
>  Content-Type: <content type>;
> boundary="randomstring"
> 
> Mail Body:
> 
>  --randomstring
>  Content-Type: text/plain; charset=us-ascii
>  Content-Disposition: inline
>  
>  this is the mail's main message.  this is not an
> attachment. your MUA
>  will display this.
>  
>  --randomstring
>  Content-Type: text/plain; charset=us-ascii
>  Content-Disposition: attachment;
> filename="attachment.txt"
>  
>  this is the content of the attachment.
>  --randomstring--
> 
>  
> Here,   the   various  portions   of   your   mail  
> starts  with   a
> --<randomstring> and the entire  stuff ends with a
> --<randomstring>--
> (note the trailing '--'s).
>

> give a small idea of
> how you can implement this:

Ravi, watch your tongue.  Abusing folks does not educate them.  Not
everyone is familiar with netiquette.  Many people today do not
understand what the subscriber's responsibilities are on a mailing
list and many are hopeless when it comes to quoting messages.  These
are not dumb people they just don't know whats wrong.  Internet access
is fairly ubiquitous these days but most folks are new to forums and
mailing lists.  Unfortunately there isn't something like an "internet
license" (like a drivers license) which ensures that anyone using it
has a basic idea of the ground rules.  Whats worse is that
knowledgeable people like you abuse them rather than gently guide them
to sites that tell them how to use mailing lists.  For instance ESR's
"How To Ask Questions The Smart Way" is an excellent read:

 http://www.tuxedo.org/~esr/faqs/smart-questions.html

I'd recommend anyone who is on a mailing list read it.

I've also been noticing a little too many off topic posts lately.  It
looks like no one reads or remembers the welcome message that is sent
when you subscribe to ilugc.  For instance programming related
questions belong on other lists a few of these on ilugc are okay but
this list was started as a FLOSS help list.  So here are the list
guidelines again.

  1. Technical queries may be posted to this list but you are likely
  to get a better response on linux-india-help@lists.sourceforge.net.
  More information on that list is available here:
  http://www.linux-india.org

  2. Please avoid flaming on this list.

  3. Please trim your replies and use quoting appropriately.

  4. Many users find HTML posts annoying so please post messages on
  this list in plain text.

  5. Please avoid posts that are not related to Linux and Open Source
  related topics.

  6. When you _have_ to send mail that is off-topic remember to
  prepend an [OT] or [Off-topic] tag to the subject.  Similarly if the
  mail involves something commercial please prepend a [Commerial] tag.


Come to think of it I think item 1 is a little too old and does not
hold anymore.  ILUGC is huge with more than 700 subscribers.  Many are
subscribed with nomail but its clear that we are a large group.  I
think technical questions on FLOSS related stuff is OK for the list
but dont push your luck with off topic queries.

cheers,
prabhu

From rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au  Thu Dec 19 09:44:27 2002
From: rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au (Raja Subramanian)
Date: Thu, 19 Dec 2002 20:44:27 +1100
Subject: [Ilugc] To check the CPU heat
In-Reply-To: <20021218153808.35604.qmail@web13708.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <200212181441.UAA23116@WS0005.indiatimes.com> <20021218153808.35604.qmail@web13708.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20021219094427.GA2820@pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au>

Hi,

Tamil Nadu wrote:
> Is there is any tool available to monitor the CPU heat
> in linux and how to reduce it if it's too high. ASUS
> has given a tool to monitor the cpu heat only in the
> windows environment. Any help will be appreciated.

Try using ACPI if possible. ACPI support is still incomplete in the
2.4.x kernels (and the 2.5.x kernels too), so you will need to plenty of
patience. The temperature sensors work fine, but features like
standby/hibernation are mostly broken.

I have a Transmeta Crusoe based notebook that runs 2.4.19 + acpi patches
and can display CPU temperature -

rsubr@igloo:~$ cat /proc/acpi/thermal_zone/THRM/temperature 
temperature:             50 C

You can drop the CPU temperature by slowing it down and reducing the
voltage. The "longrun" feature of the Crusoe can automatically regulate
CPU frequency and voltage to match CPU load. If the CPU get's too hot,
it can also be forced to operate slower.

Intel's "SpeedStep" and AMD's "PowerNow" enabled CPUs allow limited
frequency regulation.  But I don't know if you can do this without a
reboot, etc.

In any case, ACPI is the way to go.

- Raja

http://www.erserver.com/,  provides Replication feature for PostgreSQL.

Till sometime back they were offering free downloads but now they have
started charging substantially :(

Moinak.

At 04:38 PM 12/18/2002 +0530, BGanesh wrote:
>Hello,
>
>         Last week, we at ETV implemented a postgreSQL backend for 
> election results
>updates at Gujarat. There were twelve input clients, and three output clients
>which generated realtime on air graphics. Clients were all Windows 2000
>(anybody know of any good character generators ala CG2000 from matrox running
>on Linux?).
>
>         There were two Linux machines running postgresql, in an almost 
> failsafe
>environment. The secondary database would pull the most recent data every
>minute via a cron job from the primary and update itself. In case the primary
>db failed, it would shoot the primary (if it was still alive), and take over
>by a simple ip change (I know I know, there are better ways). The clients
>with uncommited transactions would rollback, and the data remains online with
>a worst case scenario of 30 seconds downtime. When the first machine came
>back online in such a scenario, it would begin functioning as the
>secondary...
>
>         What would make postgres production ready is realtime 
> replication, and I
>guess that would be available in ver 7.3 (any ETA for this?).
>
>         Downsides : The developers were from the Windows world, and made 
> certain
>incorrect assumptions (ex, setup and teardown of tables is fast in MS
>sql2000, and quite slow in postgres; and since they were unaware of this fact
>they were creating temporary tables all over the place for complex queries).
>So, the only problem was their unfamiliarity with the tools....
>
>         in a related note, is anybody aware of MS-Access like DB's for 
> Linux (as in
>ease of use) ?
>
>regards
>BGa

Hi,

     Free memory is wasted memory!  Linux dynamically allocates free memory
to serve as vaious I/O buffers to speed up I/O operations. The buffers
automatically shrink when more memory is required to run applications.

Regards,
Moinak.

| Come to think  of it I think item  1 is a little too old  and does not

`----

If ILUGC  is to talk  only about FLOSS,  maybe ILUGC could ask  ppl to
post with a '[non-free]' tag attached  to its subject when ppl talk of
non-free  software in  this  mailing list?   That  would atleast  keep
people informed  that stuff  such as Oracle  on GNU/Linux is  not Free
Software.  If a  member posts a query /  reply about non-free software
with an  appropriate '[non-free]'  tag, Free Software  enthusiasts can
continue  ignoring mails  with  a '[non-free]'  tag.   

ILUGC need  not care  explaining what the  'Free' in Free  Software is
about,  but could atleast  prevent confusion  by asking  ppl to  use a
'non-free' tag.  Many  think that stuff such as  Opera on GNU/Linux is
Free Software  and I  swear it takes  a lot  of effort from  a totally
different angle  to understand  the free (as  in freedom) nature  of a
given software.   Many donot have  the time/patience to figure  it out
and continue calling such non-free  software as Free Software and keep
the confusion spreading.

It depends on  how ILUGC defines 'free'.  If ILUGC  goes by the saying
"Freedom defined is Freedom  denied" will GPLed software be considered
free by  ILUGC? because GPL _does_  put a few  restrictions to protect
the freedom and as a result removes certain lesser important freedoms.
(as  a consequence  iLugc itself  can't exist  because even  the linux
kernel is  GPLed!  hehe...  and if  my suggestion to  add a 'non-free'
tag  is approved  by Prabhu  (or bharathi  too?),  literally everybody
posting to this list will have to use a non-free tag!)

also been enabled.

going on.

language pack for our localization and internationalization work. Since
"Latha" on Linux gives some errors during combination, we would like to
have inputs on better OpenType fonts for Tamil.

In-Reply-To: <20021219111626.30189.qmail@web11103.mail.yahoo.com>

mohammedshaikabdullah abdullah wrote on Thu, Dec 19, 2002 at 03:16:26AM -0800: 

,----
| Am  new  to  the world  of  linux.  please  instruct  me How  to  make
| partinion, How to install linux,  how to configure Ethernetcard and do
| other configuration i have lotof doubt please any one help learn about
| linux
`----

Welcome to this wonderful world of GNU/Linux and Free Software! We are
here to  help people who utter  'what the heck?' when  they hear about
partitioning and swap spaces and -what-not-buzz- words. :)

Before science, a bit of history...

the popular OS that you find everywhere and called as 'Linux' actually
fits  itself into  a project  called the  'GNU (GNUs  Not  Unix)'. GNU
started in  1984 to provide  a completely free operating  system.  The
free here  refers to the Freedom  that it gives (freedom  to study the
source code, modify it and share it) and not the 'free-of-cost'ness.

in 1991, Linus Torvalds wrote a kernel named 'Linux'. GNU at that time
did not  have a  functional kernel  and hence GNU  and Linux  was used
together to become a  fully usable Operating System named 'GNU/Linux'.
GNU     also    has     its    own     kernel    named     the    HURD
(http://gnu.org/software/hurd/) which is based  on a much more complex
and extensible 'microkernel' approach.

Now for your questions:

Partitioning is done with tools  like fdisk, cfdisk, etc.,. There is a
wonderful partitioning tutorial at:

http://www.linuxplanet.com/linuxplanet/tutorials/3174/6/

Most  GNU/Linux distributions  have an  installation guide  (some even
have nice screenshots!). explore your installation CDROM :)

Network  card configuration is  generally in  two parts...  1. telling
your kernel  what driver  drives your network  card. 2. setting  up IP
Address, routing information, etc.,.

There are  wonderful (no I'm not  telling lies.. ;) )  man pages which
explain  these:   

 modules.conf(5) -  modules configuration files  (also as conf.modules
 in some GNU/Linux distributions)
 modules(5) - file  containing the list of modules  to load at startup
 (only on debian?)
 lsmod(8) - list the current loaded modules
 insmod(8) - insert a specified module
 modprobe(8) - insert a module and all its dependencies
 ifconfig(8) - configure your network card's IP Address, etc.,.

    -Suraj

On Thu, Dec 19, 2002 at 12:28:22PM +0000, slash_axl_rose_upen wrote:
> hi all
> how to use gpg in linux
> can i use it for encrypting data in mails sent from my
> workstation ??if yes...
> HOW/????
> please mail on my id the procedure...thnx in advance

(michael@bevilacqua) $ gpg -r "User ID" -e filename

=2E..will encrypt your message as filename.gpg

(michael@bevilacqua) $ gpg --decrypt filename.gpg

=2E..will decrypt filename.gpg

(michael@bevilacqua) $ man gpg

=2E..will give you more on this

Hello,

	I have been looking at various resources on the web for Indian Language 
support (fonts, keyboards and applications), but each seems to be pulling in 
different direction. Even ISCII and Unicode seem to disagree *sigh*. 

	I would like to see multilingual Indian language support under X / Linux and 
am willing to devote some resources to these.. if there are some standards 
that can be followed that would be helpful. Also, if the people on the list 
who seem to have managed Tamil support could provide pointers I would be 
grateful.

Mandrake 9 provides fairly decent tamil support (if a touch too literate
for my poor knowledge of tamil ... the tamil used there sounds very
textbookish / over-literate).

You get yourself a decent keymap for tamil and star office for tamil

package.

I dont remember the context but a few years back, one of my friends, who is
not Indian, asked me, but why does Indian media pay so much attention to it?
By paying attention, you have given them the publicity, they desired. 
About 8 months back, in ILUGC mailing list, I had mailed(after reading
40+(by a very conservative guess) mails on asking a new joinee not to waste
precious bandwidth for some reason(again my poor memory fails me.) )  asking
people how much band-width we have wasted by sending back and forth so many
mails. I know perhaps what I am writing wont make much sense, but we can do
better by ignoring such mails in the future. Ofcourse its individuals
choice.
 
Thanks,
Anoop.

Message-ID: <F150qqNXd0jCQPrE6hF0002e213@hotmail.com>

Hi,
I think it is better to use the write() call than the send() with TCP 
sockets, especially when you are sending structures. Invoke as
write(sockDescptr,(char*)&structure,sizeof(structure));

rgds,Prashanth

From arvind_7 at kongu.ac.in  Fri Dec 20 15:02:16 2002
From: arvind_7 at kongu.ac.in (Arvind Kalyan)
Date: Fri, 20 Dec 2002 20:32:16 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] mysql with c/c++
In-Reply-To: <F27umY1IaNrvpxmTi3I0002e509@hotmail.com>
References: <F27umY1IaNrvpxmTi3I0002e509@hotmail.com>
Message-ID: <20021220203216.M9267@mail.kongu.ac.in>

> hallo, 
> Kindly mention the sample example program of mysql connectivity with 
c/c++.  regards,

read about the mysql API. its very simple...

you create a connection with the server with mysql_connect() and then  issue 
commands using mysql_query() and retrieve the rows using mysql_fetch_rows() 
function. use the manual that you got with the mysql distribution.

example source code for clients can also be found under the base dir of your 
mysql source direvtory.

> kk

o GNU/LINUX UTILITIES FOR EDUCATION... GLUE: Ajith Kumar
<ajith@nsc.ernet.in> deserves credit for his work on this front. Recently,
Ajith announced that his product -- the "GNU Linux Utilities for Education"
CD is now hosted at "ftp.seul.org". This is a bootable CD that will install
a GNU/Linux system with OpenOffice, several educational software packages
and the Terminal Server Software "within 10 minutes", as he puts it.  Ajith
needs help in testing. You can download the ISO image from
ftp://ftp.seul.org/pub/glue/ Bowse the contents of it at
ftp://ftp.seul.org/pub/glue/GLUE/index.html

Recently, Ajith was demoing the CD to the Press. Says he: "It takes only 10
minutes to setup the lab. Method is extreamly simple. Create a RedHat (or
any other) installation and all other required software. Make a tarball of
it. A bootable CD with a small script plants it to another computer. "Kudzu"
does a good job in detecting new hardware." Free Software campaigners in the
Southern State of Kerala are convinced that the local government is "wasting
their money" if they sign a MoU (memorandum of understanding) for costly
proprietorial software to be implemented in their IT@School Project.

o MAKING FREE SOFTWARE/OPEN SOURCE A 'HOUSEHOLD NAME': Abhishek
<efylinux1@electronicsforu.com> of ElectronicsForYou magazine writes in to
announce the planned launch of a new Indian mag, devoted entirely to Free
Software and Open Source. Some key facts, as promised by this publishing
group, are as follows. Launch date: mid January 2003. Pages: 100 plus. Cover
price: Rs 50, or about US$1 (including a CD).

	This mag is likely to be called 'Linux For You'. It is being
	published by the same group that brings out 'Electronics For You'
	and the 'i.t.' magazines. Ideas, suggestions, doubts and inputs
	for editorial content invited. 

o LINUX-INDIA GENERAL: This is the list which still is working to play the
role of networking different Free/Libre and Open Source Software initiatives
across India. See the Linux-India General list at
https://lists.sourceforge.net/lists/listinfo/linux-india-general

o LITTLE LEAGUE: The idea is to help smaller LUGs around India to network
and share resources and ideas to grow and survive. If you belong to this
category, contact Sukrit D of Pondicherry <sd_root@yahoo.com>. There's also
an offer to help you get inexpensive (maybe even zero-cost) CDs of useful
distros... provided you undertake to share the same widely in your area.

	o BELGAUM LUG: Belgaum is a city of c. 300,000 in North Karnataka
	and home to one of the youngest GNU/Linux user groups in India.
	This was recently launched with most members being students of
	the Gogte College of Engineering there. If you'd like to get in
	touch contact Ashutosh Naik <a7ash@yahoo.com> and Rohan
	Kangralkar <rohankangralkar@hotmail.com>. See also their list at
	http://groups.yahoo.com/group/ilug-belgaum All the best to them.

o LINKING STUDENTS, PROJECTS, MENTORS: Mumbai/Bombay-based Trevor Warren
<trevorwarren@yahoo.com> or <trevor.w@media.mit.edu>, while still in his
early twenties, has come up with this idea of a Project Resource Centre. The
goal? To link students wanting socially-useful and challenging projects with
techies willing to play the role of mentors. Any volunteers?

Says Warren: "As of now...we are looking forwards to having a decent site
dissimanating information to the FSF/OS community on the following aspects.
--> What is the objective of the PRC. --> List of projects for (students) to
take up --> List of mentors with their skill sets (based on a Wiki-like
tool) --> List of projects students/community wants to propose --> Section
for commercial projects that the industry wants to offer --> Collabration
tool for all.

	Tripta <tripta@sarai.net> from Delhi, another young lady behind
	a lot of interesting work, volunteered to list some of the people
	who have already signed up at the PRC as mentors, some possible
	projects, and who's coming forward to work on the same. 

For more details, sign on or check out the archives at the site
http://mail.sarai.net/mailman/listinfo/prc

From info5 at csl.cc  Sat Dec 21 20:29:33 2002
From: info5 at csl.cc (Consorcio Software Libre)
Date: Sat, 21 Dec 2002 14:29:33 -0600
Subject: [Ilugc] [Off-Topic] Free Software Consortium in search of Consultants and Agents in your area.
Message-ID: <E18PunO-00019j-00@barrier.vosn.net>

We would like to invite you to be a founding members of the FSC either as a
Consultant and/or an Agent.

http://www.fsconsortium.com

On the main page you will find links to subscribe as consultant and/or agent.

Free Software Consortium is a multinational consortium established to link the
companies and the independent consultants that use and promote free software.

One of the bigger obstacles to the development of the free software services
market is the fear of many companies to establish contracts with independent
consultants who do not have support of a well known Company, Corporation or
Consortium.  Questioning quality, support, experience and capability to
successfully complete a project are the companies manager's main concerns when
considering the option of migrating their systems to free software.

Like you, we know the excellent quality that Free Software offers.
We have complete confidence that Free Software is going to be the platform of
the future. That is why it's so important to work and consolidate together to
solve the problem mentioned above.

Free Software Consortium intends to fill this void joining the best free
software companies and consultants at the national and international level.

By joining to Free Software Consortium you or your company will have the
following benefits:

1. Possibility of being hired by other Consortium members.
2. Possibility of hiring other Consortium members.
3. Use of the Consortium image and name with your clients.
4. Use of the Consortium's resources like Publicity Brochures, Business Cards,
Banners for presentations and events, financial presentations, publicity
articles for the press and magazines, support via mailing list and forums with
the Consortium's members, marketing and communication assistance, CD's and
manuals from the Consortium, site and mail hosting (yourarea.fsc.cc) and other
future services.
5. Representation of the FS Consortium in your area to share administrative,
legal and marketing resources between the Consultant members in your area.

Free Software Consortium will establish a contract with an Agent company which
will have exclusive representation in it's area, in charge of organizing the
consultants in the area.  This Agent company will provide the administrative
services, marketing and sales with the local customers.

>From the business generated by the Free Software Consortium, the Agent company
will receive 20% of the value of the contract, and the Consultant or 
Consulting
company will receive 80%.

The Free Software Consortium is developing a new business model and invites 
you
to join as a founding member and contribute in developing this new business
model.  We need your valuable help to give us ideas and comments. Please write
to info@fsconsortium.com


Thank you for your attention.


Free Software Consortium
http://www.fsconsortium.com
info@fsc.cc


From sriram at aero.iitm.ernet.in  Sun Dec 22 12:45:12 2002
From: sriram at aero.iitm.ernet.in (sriram@aero.iitm.ernet.in)
Date: Sun, 22 Dec 2002 18:15:12 +0530 (IST)
Subject: [Ilugc] GUI login in Redhat 8.0
Message-ID: <1119.202.56.193.48.1040561112.squirrel@www.aero.iitm.ernet.in>

On Sat, 21 Dec 2002, Tamil Nadu wrote:
>

> I don't want to give 777 authorization to "tmp" directory. How to allow
other users to login with tmp authorization as 755. (tmp owner & group
is root). Any suggestions will be greatly appreciated.

h

in general, it is a bad idea to deny users write access to tmp directory.
it is temporary space, right? if you are concerned about disk usage, put
quotas. if you dont want quotas, but simply want tmp not to have junk,
use the tmpwatch facility. redhat 8 has a reasonably configured tmpwatch,
tweak it as needed. if you really dont want to do these but want users
to work with x, create an orbit-foo directory for each user foo. this
directory should be owned by user foo who should have rwx permits to it
(700 will work fine). x will work fine for users after this. it is also
possible to reconfig so orbit will use the users' home directory instead
of /tmp.

sriram

Hi Venki, 
U can log into the single user mode and make the system "rw" and change the password.

If u are using GRUB.just when the GRUB displays the lists of Kernels @bootup,just press 'e' ,this will take u to the restricted version of the shell.GRUB showing a command..
It will be something like //"GRUB>kernel....

At the end of the command add 'init=/bin/sh" and then enter

and then continue with the loading of the System..
It will take u to the 
# prompt..where the system is read only..

U can change the password of the root..from here...after making rw 

ASFAIK,this works for me.

Gurus,Correct me if this does not work...

Thanks 
Giridharan

 venki <avenkatesh79@rediffmail.com> wrote:i forgot root passwd in my gnu/linux based RH. is it possible to reset the 
root passwd? if yes, how can i do so? Thanks in advance.

From sangeeth_10 at yahoo.com  Mon Dec 23 06:00:55 2002
From: sangeeth_10 at yahoo.com (Sangeetha)
Date: Sun, 22 Dec 2002 22:00:55 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [Ilugc] root passwd
In-Reply-To: <200212231037.30309.avenkatesh79@rediffmail.com>
Message-ID: <20021223060055.67914.qmail@web13305.mail.yahoo.com>

hi,
   even i faced with similar problem...jus boot in
single user mode by giving 'linux single' at the
prompt where u choose between linux or win os.....open
up the file /etc/shadow....in the entry for root
delete the encrypted msg between first two
colons...then at the prompt give init 3(console
booting) or init 5 (x windows)....u can get inside jus
specifying the username(root) and need not specify the
pswd....then assign a pswd for root.

hope this workd out.

Sangeetha

From ragu at vsnl.com  Mon Dec 23 06:02:35 2002
From: ragu at vsnl.com (Raghavendra Bhat)
Date: Mon, 23 Dec 2002 11:32:35 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] root passwd
In-Reply-To: <3E06EE50.200612BF@npd.hcltech.com>
References: <200212231037.30309.avenkatesh79@rediffmail.com> <3E06EE50.200612BF@npd.hcltech.com>
Message-ID: <20021223060235.GA664@gnuhead>

Subrahmanya posts :

>> Boot your linux in single user  mode.  At the shell, you can change
             ^^^^^

>>
>> venki wrote:
>>
>>> i forgot root  passwd in my gnu/linux based RH.  is it possible to
>>> reset the root passwd ?

The OP  knows what the system  is called as.   You do not even  have a
clue and should read this http://www.gnu.org/gnu/why-gnu-linux.html

The  later  distros of  GNU/Linux,  particularly  a former  brain-dead
Redhat has woken up.  You may  not get shell access in `linux single'.
So what do you do ?

Mount root  partition and cd  to /etc.  Load  nano or vi and  open the
file `passwd'.  It will look like this

root:nTrVnuRFhSbGg:12022:0:99999:7:::
     ^^^^^^^^^^^^^

Null the highlighted characters alone, be careful.  Save the file and
reboot.  Just pressing the `Enter' key would let you in as root.  Fix
the password by doing `passwd'.

If you have  enabled shadow password, the file  to edit is /etc/shadow
instead.  Look behind your back......

From itmani at hotmail.com  Mon Dec 23 17:00:20 2002
From: itmani at hotmail.com (Manikandan P.)

Hi

> i forgot root passwd in my gnu/linux based RH. is it possible to reset the
> root passwd? if yes, how can i do so? Thanks in advance.

boot into your system by typing
#linux 1
at the boot prompt
you will be landing at the root prompt.
#passwd -d root
now give
init <runlevel>


Happy Hacking
Manikandan P.

single" in RH Gnu/Linux to boot in single user mode
(It has failed for me). If you have rescue floppy,
boot from it and edit /etc/passwd file.

Edit the second column marked "x" and remove it. Then
reboot the system and when you get the login prompt,
type "root" and you will get the shell prompt. Then
change the root password using 'passwd' command.

Regards,
Guru Prasad.

Hello,

	Select the country East Europe and reception as PAL. You can use
'zapping' instead of xawtv which is very flexible. The best feature I
like in zapping is that you can tune channels which belong to different
countries (i.e i can also have channels which come under the US or
Japan). This isn't possible in xawtv since you'll be stuck with one
country setting. Alternatively you can also try kwintv which has similar
feature sets and also has an option to tune the channels manually.

hello all,


I am posting this mail not just as an ilugc member but also in the capacity of the general secretary of the Association Of Computer Engineers of Sri venkateshwara College Of Engineering, Sriperumbudur.As part of the yearly activities of the association , it is customary to organize guest lectures on topics of technical intererst to computer engineers.Being a guest lecture and keeping in mind the time constraint( about an hour or so ) ,i would like to make an open request to experienced proffessionals who are members of ilugc to deliver one of such guest lectures at the college premises. I hate to sound picky , but there are a few things that should be kept in mind 

>> the lec-dem is definitely technical , but not overly so ,so that it caters to the average student.

>> It would be wonderful , if the speaker could also mention of opportunities in the area , as well as projects that are being implemented etc. so as to serve as an inspiration to the young proffessionals.This is especially important as, most of these 3rd year engineers are still groping in the dark regarding their future.

>> S.V.C.E is one of the leading engineering colleges in the city , and its C.S.E department has loads of talent ,therefore , the speaker is guaranteed an intelligent, attentive audience

>> The lec-dem will be held sometime next week , so it will be great if someone can come forward and meet this great opportunity to interact with students on a one-to-one basis , and respond to this mail along with a few necessary details etc. like what the lecture will be about , and when you can be free to deliver it etc. to my personal e-mail i.d.
Lot's of leading members from the industry have spoken at the college and i thought that the moment is right to infuse a more pragmatic approach to this entire lec-dem approach by calling someone who actually codes and the students might be able to relate to.I hope that , a few of you will defintely come forward and avail of this opportunity to deliver a lecture at S.V.C.E

regards
Aditya Krishnan

From jvijay at imagine.co.in  Thu Dec 26 05:03:32 2002
From: jvijay at imagine.co.in (J. Vijay Kumar)
Date: Thu, 26 Dec 2002 10:33:32 +0530 (IST)
Subject: [Ilugc] reg adding new hard disk.
In-Reply-To: <5.2.0.9.0.20021226100202.01444ff0@mail.roc.co.in>
References: <5.2.0.9.0.20021226100202.01444ff0@mail.roc.co.in>
Message-ID: <1802.192.168.100.20.1040879012.squirrel@mail.imagine.co.in>

you should create a filesystem using mkfs. The command shall be as follows.
# mkfs /dev/hdb (if its connect as secondary master)
After that edit /etc/fstab
/dev/hdb /home2 ext2 defults 0 0 ( I am not sure about the numbers after
default)
Else you can use a 'mount /dev/hdb /home2' for time-being/

From ragu at vsnl.com  Thu Dec 26 05:05:12 2002
From: ragu at vsnl.com (Raghavendra Bhat)
Date: Thu, 26 Dec 2002 10:35:12 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] reg adding new hard disk.

References: <5.2.0.9.0.20021226100202.01444ff0@mail.roc.co.in>
Message-ID: <20021226050512.GA9843@gnuhead>

sathish posts :

>> when i am fdisk adding new partition  , i am not able to mount that
>> partition

First partition  the new HDD  using fdisk, then format  the partitions
using mke2fs.  Read `man mke2fs' and `man fdisk'.


>> /dev/hdb	/home2		ext2		defaults	  1 1
        ^^^

You can  only mount partitions within  a HDD.  You  have not specified
which partition, just mentioning the drive is not enough.

Instead of hdb, use hdb1 or hdb2 or whatever.....


>> this was  the line  i added in  fstab the  message i am  getting is
>> invalid file system.

Sure you would.  Mention the slice number instead of the drive alone.

From basker at india.hp.com  Thu Dec 26 18:31:34 2002
From: basker at india.hp.com (Basker.P)
Date: Thu, 26 Dec 2002 13:31:34 -0500 (EST)
Subject: [Ilugc] user structure
In-Reply-To: <20021226061249.64889.qmail@web13302.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0212261318480.2784-100000@einstein.india.hp.com>

>    Can anyone plz tell where i can find the User
> structure of current process (in which path) in linux
> ...like where is the user structure delared....so that
> i can ref members like
> u_error,u_uid,u_base,u_count,u_offset .

Looks like ur trying to correlate traditional unix kernel with linux
kernel architecture. Traditional unix has uarea and proc as separate
entities. Linux doesn't.  In linux both the uarea and proc are clubbed
together in the task_struct structure. Instead of u.field, u can access
the fields of interest as current->field. This is different from the
"CURRENT" macro in block device driver code. Now dont ask me where the
pregion and address space structures are! Just follow ur instincts while u 
browse the code and have some linux kernel book handy.

	P.Basker

> Sangeetha

From mallet at efn.org  Thu Dec 26 10:23:28 2002
From: mallet at efn.org (Suresh Ramasubramanian)
Date: Thu, 26 Dec 2002 15:53:28 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] Beep Sound
References: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0212261424100.631-100000@lantana.iitm.ernet.in>
Message-ID: <001301c2acc8$e5060990$0201a8c0@quirk>

On Thursday, December 26, 2002 2:28 PM [GMT+0530=IST],
bharathi@lantana.TeNeT.res.in (Bharathi S) wrote:

>  Some our machines makes loud beep sound.
>  How to reduce the sound from Console Mode ?

Try this -

#!/bin/sh
if [ "$1" = "off" ]; then
        echo -e "\33[11;0]"
        echo "Bell turned off."
fi

if [ "$1" = "on" ]; then
        echo -e "\33[10;750]\33[11;250]"
        echo "Bell turned on."
fi

if [ "$1" = "" ]; then
        echo "Usage: $0 <on|off>"
fi


    srs

From egrpbala at yahoo.com  Thu Dec 26 13:51:30 2002
From: egrpbala at yahoo.com (Bala)
Date: Thu, 26 Dec 2002 05:51:30 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [Ilugc] reg adding new hard disk.
In-Reply-To: <20021226050512.GA9843@gnuhead>
Message-ID: <20021226135130.48880.qmail@web11101.mail.yahoo.com>

 /dev/hdb	/home2		ext2		defaults	  1 1

the fifth and sixth fields are dump and fsck, if the
fifth field is 
zero, the file system will not be dumped, sixth field
is used to determine the order of the filesystem check
(fsck) at reboot time, usually for root filesystem the
sixth field is 1 for others 2, if it is 0 the
filesystem will not be checked.

   see $man fstab     for more details

-bala-

From rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au  Fri Dec 27 01:15:50 2002
From: rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au (Raja Subramanian)
Date: Fri, 27 Dec 2002 12:15:50 +1100
Subject: [Ilugc] reg adding new hard disk.
In-Reply-To: <20021226050512.GA9843@gnuhead>
References: <5.2.0.9.0.20021226100202.01444ff0@mail.roc.co.in> <20021226050512.GA9843@gnuhead>
Message-ID: <20021227011550.GA29501@pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au>

Raghavendra Bhat wrote:
> sathish posts :
> 
> >> when i am fdisk adding new partition  , i am not able to mount that
> >> partition
> 
> First partition  the new HDD  using fdisk, then format  the partitions
> using mke2fs.  Read `man mke2fs' and `man fdisk'.
> 
> 
> >> /dev/hdb	/home2		ext2		defaults	  1 1
>         ^^^
> 
> You can  only mount partitions within  a HDD.  You  have not specified
> which partition, just mentioning the drive is not enough.
> 

Not really. You can create a filesystem (and mount it) on *any* block
device. You can certainly use the entire disk (eg. /dev/hdb) to create a
filesystem and not bother with partitions.

However, this approach is not recommended as some disk
partitioning/diagnostic programs may think that it is an uninitialised
disk and create a new partition table.

This could cause much headache as it overwrites the first few critical
blocks of the filesystem. It's far safer to partition first, and then
create filesystems.

- Raja

Hi,

Intel 845 Chipset family is supported in the XFree86 3.0 and above that too
in CVS only. The official release for the same is yet happen. Try
downloading the Source and re-compiling. You can use the 845 Chipset by
configuring the Video Card to VESA along with the Motherboard BIOS setting
of Video Memory changed to 8 MB from the default 1 MB.

Hope this helps.

From bhuvanbk at myrealbox.com  Fri Dec 27 09:22:41 2002
From: bhuvanbk at myrealbox.com (Bhuvan A)
Date: Fri, 27 Dec 2002 14:52:41 +0530 (IST)
Subject: [Ilugc] postgresql with php ?
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0212251520480.22375-100000@mrna.tn.nic.in>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0212271445420.1775-100000@Bhuvan.bksys.co.in>


> hi all,
> How to use PHP with postgresql ?  doi need to have to mention any such
> support  for postgresql while compilation of postgresql?

No need to re-compile postgresql. Rather you can do any one of the 
following.

a. Re-compile php with '--with-pgsql' option while configuring 
b. Have pgsql.so as dynamic loadable library. It can be done by
uncommenting the below line in /etc/php.ini

;extension=pgsql.so

regards,
bhuvaneswaran



From sriram at aero.iitm.ernet.in  Fri Dec 27 09:18:27 2002
From: sriram at aero.iitm.ernet.in (P. Sriram)
Date: Fri, 27 Dec 2002 14:48:27 +0530 (IST)
Subject: [Ilugc] Mirroring Deb packages!
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0212271136440.2458-100000@Uday.bksys.co.in>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0212271416180.6485-100000@gateway.aero.iitm.ernet.in>

On Fri, 27 Dec 2002, Udaya kumar.R wrote:
>    We have planned to set up a deb mirror site. So, i was on the deb site
>    I have done some homework on this, and i hope people would go through 
> it and respond with their suggestions.

> * Space allocated 2.0 GB
> * Mirroring only i386 binary packages.
> * Gona to use rsync, as it seems to be the widely used one.

even with i386 binaries only, i dont believe 2gb will be adequate. the 
iitm mirror includes sources and binaries for i386 only and it is 26gb. 
daily update traffic is around 150-200 megabytes (100mb or so min, max 
around 400mb). because of the directory structures used, it would be 
madness to try anything other than rsync. the debian site has a sample 
script which you can tune appropriately. you can use the netselect program 
to find the 'fastest' site for you. we used to do from planetmirror in 
australia but lately, that site has become too slow. australia is a good 
bet since cron job run late at night ist are early morning in australia 
but peak time in europe and usa - but that logic is not holding anymore. 
we are mirroring from kernel.org and i am getting anything from 25 - 75 
kilobytes per hour. i doubt if luggies will be interested in more details 
- we can continue the thread in private.

From: bharathi at lantana.TeNeT.res.in (Bharathi S)
Date: Fri, 27 Dec 2002 17:30:57 +0530 (IST)
Subject: [ilugc] Indian Language support under GNU\Linux / X
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0212271707160.10497-100000@lantana.iitm.ernet.in>

Hello Mr BGanesh and All,

Here is a short(!?) summary of our IndLinuX Team work:

Today the TeNeT Group (IIT-Madras) is involved in the wide scale
deployment of Internet kiosks across the countryside.  The kiosks
require local language software so that they can be effectively used
by the marginalized literate population of OUR country.

Given the number of Indian languages and different encoding standards
and fonts they use, it was felt that we need to develop Indian
language support that is essentially INDEPENDENT OF ENCODING & FONT.

Further, we felt that this support must be provided at the kernel /
X-Window system levels so that applications that run on top of the
kernel/X-Window system INHERIT the interface.

To this end we provide TWO different solutions under GNU Linux: kernel
based and X-Window based.

> Kernel based solution: 

Indian languages have variable width characters. To support variable
width at the kernel level, a multi-glyph approach is proposed, i.e. a
keystroke may correspond to one or more glyphs. Further, the number of
keystrokes possible on the standard QWERTY keyboard is not sufficient
to represent all characters and character clusters in any given
language.  This results in the problem that a sequences of keys may
correspond to different glyphs (in that a key sequence AB might
correspond to a glyph G1, while a key sequence ABC might correspond to
a different glyph G2). This requires that the system has a memory of
the keystrokes that have been made.  To address this problem a finite
state machine and a set of associated rules was introduced in the
kernel.

> X-Window based solution:  

Two different solutions are supported at the X-Window level, namely,
glyph based and encoding based.  In the first approach, similar to
that of the kernel, the parsing is done on the input side, while
glyphs are produced on the output side (file/display).  In this
approach, clearly the system is tied to the font that is used.  To
overcome this problem, an encoding based solution has also been
provided.  The problem with this approach is in cursor positioning.  
The position of the cursor is maintained by the application which
interacts with X to obtain the widths of characters.  The cursor is
positioned based on the keys typed (no memory/context sensitivity is
assumed). We are yet to address this problem.  We do feel that the
only solution available to us is to provide a set of cursor APIs in X
which can be used by any application.

In either solution, the language dependent information is provided in
parse rule tables.  This information is loaded at runtime.  This
ensures that changing the local language environment is SIMPLY a
question of manipulating parse rule tables.

> Applications:  

The solutions that we have provided enable a user to type in a local
language in most applications (Open Office/ KOffice/gcc...).  We have
further customized some of the applications (menus/errors in local
languages), namely, KOffice, Konqueror, gcc, pine, emacs.  We are
currently working on customising Open Office. We are also working on a
convertor which converts indian language documents from fonts to
encoding, fonts to fonts, encoding to font and it can also do
translitration across indian languages

> Current Support:

 Tamil (Glyph-based) - TamilNet99, Inscript
 Hindi (Glyph-based) - Inscript

 Tamil (Encoding-based) - ISCII
 Hindi (Encoding-based) - ISCII

The above supports are complete (This simply means that we have
populated the appropriate language dependent parse rule files). We are
currently working on Malayalam, Oriya, Marathi and Gujarathi.

> Major Bugs

  o Cursor position problem
  o Few Memory leakages

> Future Plans:

This work is part of a MAJOR PLAN to develop a MULTI-MODAL interface
to the computer.  By MULTI-MODAL, we mean, handwriting, keyboard and
speech interfaces.  We have started work on both handwriting and
speech.  We have developed a handwriting interface for Tamil and have
developed speech technology software for: Speech synthesis in Tamil,
Hindi, Telugu and Malayalam (Malayalam database was obtained from
ISDL, Trivandrum). Spoken language Identification, Syllable-based
recognition of continuous speech, Speaker identification.

Web Site : http://www.tenet.res.in/Donlab/Indlinux/   
  ( Currently reconstruction is going on)

Send ur Comments and Suggestions : indlinux@lantana.TeNeT.res.in

Thanks,
---
Bharathi S, IndLinuX Team, (__)
DONLab,     TeNeT Group,   oo /
IIT-Madras, Chennai-INDIA. (_/\

Subject: [Ilugc] Beep Sound
In-Reply-To: <001301c2acc8$e5060990$0201a8c0@quirk>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0212261424100.631-100000@lantana.iitm.ernet.in> <001301c2acc8$e5060990$0201a8c0@quirk>
Message-ID: <20021227130948.GA17665@cmi.ac.in>

Hi,

	I have added a bit more details (comments) to srs' script.

#---------------------- Script Begins -------------------#
#!/bin/sh
if [ "$1" = "off" ]; then
        echo -e "\33[11;0]"
        echo "Bell turned off."
fi

if [ "$1" = "on" ]; then
        echo -e "\33[10;750]\33[11;250]"
        echo "Bell turned on."

# The escape sequence \33[10;f] sets the frequency to f.

# And \33[11;d] sets the duration for which the speaker 
# generates the frequency f upon every beep to d.


fi

if [ "$1" = "" ]; then
        echo "Usage: $0 <on|off>"
fi
#---------------------- END of Script -------------------#

Hi,

	You may not always land up at the root prompt!

	By default GNU/Linux/Debian (let me be safe) systems start up 
slogin and not bash. Which means you need root password to boot into 
single user mode.

	If single user mode fails, then you may try using a rescue floppy.
Or an installation CD-Rom (choose rescue mode).

	Well, there's another neat way to do it by using the other kernel 
parameters! Go ahead and read the docs to find out!


On Mon, Dec 23, 2002 at 11:00:20AM -0600, Manikandan P. wrote:
> Hi
> 
> > i forgot root passwd in my gnu/linux based RH. is it possible to reset the
> > root passwd? if yes, how can i do so? Thanks in advance.
> 
> boot into your system by typing
> #linux 1
> at the boot prompt
> you will be landing at the root prompt.
> #passwd -d root
> now give
> init <runlevel>
>

GNU/LINUX TO GET A BOOST VIA PUNE: This message is from students at
Pune. We wish them all the best. Contact navhindhanuka at hotmail dot
com: "We the students of 'Symbiosis Institute of Computer Studies and
Research' (SICSR) want to contribute to the GNU project. With this aim in
mind, we are organizing 'GNUnify', with the whole hearted support of the
management of our institute." Set up in 1971, primarily to promote world
understanding between Indian and foreign students through education,
Symbiosis has a strength of over 16,000 students from over 32
countries. Says the institution: "We in Symbiosis believe that the 'World
is one Family'."

The annual fest of SICSR 'Unify', is composed of various cultural, academic
events & contests. This year the institution is adding on GNUnify, as their
own way "of contributing and encouraging the Free Software movement".

See http://www.sicsr.ac.in (to be updated by early Jan 2003)

The aim of GNUnify is to unify and encourage efforts of GNU developers
across the country, by "awarding the best and motivating the rest". Events
will include: 

1. Code-Presentations (open for all)
1.1 App Dev (Web Apps, Biz Apps, Edu Capsules)
1.2 Embedded Linux
1.3 Network Programming
1.4 Kernel Development / Device Drivers

2. Paper-Presentations (open only for students)
2.1 General (Socio-economic aspects of using GNU/Linux, Does GNU/Linux make
sense for India?, and Will China get ahead of India using Free Software?)
2.2 Free Software B-Plan Contest: The major concern of most developers is
that since GNU is free there is little / no money to be earned out it.  To
disprove this a free s/w or gnu based B-plan contest. People submit their
B-plans built around free s/w.
2.3 Technical (how to use Apache, migrating from ASP to PHP, Wirel)
3. Techie-Talks (under planning... if you know of any powerful speakers from
across the country, do suggest)
4. Hands-on Workshops [Under Planning]
5. Install-Fest of GNU/Linux [Debian, Redhat, Slackware, Mandrake, ...]
6. Screenings. [RMS's Public Lecture @ IIT-Mumbai & Linux-The Code Movie] 
Event Dates: 15 & 16 Feb 2003
E-Mail: gnunify@symbiosiscomputers.com

NEWS FROM KERALA: Arun M <arun at freedevelopers dot net> reports that he
had a recent meet with the general secretary of the KSTA, the trade union of
teachers in the southern Indian state of Kerala. They're planning a meet on
IT education in schools, and want experts to talk about Free Software.

Meanwhile, Kerala's IT@School expert committee met and seems agreeable to
the view that Free Software must be used for the project. Logistical issues
of training, text books, and distribution CDs etc need to be taken up. Help
is needed for rewriting the textbooks, in a way that these don't exclusively
promote proprietorial software.

INDIAN-LANGUAGE SOLUTIONS FROM PIONEERS AT IIT-MADRAS: 

Dr Hema A Murthy <hema at lantana dot tenet dot res dot in>, associate
professor at the IIT Madras (Chennai) is one of the two coordinators of the
IndLinux effort, along with Timothy A Gonsalves <tag at tenet dot res dot
in>. You can also contact indlinux at tenet dot res dot in for information.

She recently wrote in to point to some of the shortcomings in an article
written recently. Our apologies for an inadequate representation; we have no
excuse other than the general difficulties in garnering information across
a virtual sub-continent, largely depending on e-mail. 

Says Dr Murthy: "Currently, the TeNeT group is involved in the wide scale
deployment of Internet kiosks across the countryside.  The kiosks require
local language software so that they can be effectively used by the
marginalised literate population of our country."

We are grateful for the explanation below to Dr Murthy:

Given the number of Indian languages and different encoding standards and
fonts they use, it was felt that we need to develop Indian language support
that is essentially independent of encoding and font.  Further, we felt that
this support must be provided at the kernel/X-Window system levels so that
applications that run on top of the kernel/X-Window system inherit the
interface.

To this end we provide two different solutions under linux: kernel based 
and X-Window based. 

Kernel based solution:  Indian languages have variable width characters. To
support variable width at the kernel level, a multiglyph approach is
proposed, i.e. a keystroke may correspond to one or more glyphs. Further,
the number of keystrokes possible on the standard QWERTY keyboard is not
sufficient to represent all characters and character clusters in any given
language.  This results in the problem that a sequences of keys may
correspond to different glyphs (in that a key sequence ab might correspond
to a glyph g1, while a key sequence abc might correspond to a different
glyph g2). This requires that the system has a memory of the keystrokes that
have been made.  To address this problem a finite state machine and a set of
associated rules was introduced in the kernel.

X-Window based solution:  Two different solutions are supported at the
X-Window level, namely, glyph based and encoding based.  In the first
approach, similar to that of the kernel, the parsing is done on the input
side, while glyphs are produced on the output side (file/display).  In this
approach, clearly the system is tied to the font that is used.  To overcome
this problem, an encoding based solution has also been provided.  The
problem with this approach is in cursor positioning.  The position of the
cursor is maintained by the application which interacts with X to obtain the
widths of characters.  The cursor is positioned based on the keys typed (no
memory/context sensitivity is assumed). We are yet to address this problem. 
We do feel that the only solution available to us is to provide a set of
cursor APIs in X which can be used by any application.

In either solution, the language dependent information is provided in parse
rule tables.  This information is loaded at runtime.  This ensures that
changing the local language environment is simply a question of manipulating
parse rule tables.

Applications:  The solutions that we have provided enable a user to type in
a local language in most applications (Open Office/ KOffice/gcc...).  We
have further customised some of the applications (menus/errors in local
languages), namely, KOffice, Konqueror, gcc, pine, emacs.  We are currently
working on customising Open Office. We are also working on a convertor from
fonts to encoding, fonts to fonts, encoding to font.

Current Support:   Tamil  (Glyph-based) - TamilNet99, Inscript
                   Hindi  (Glyph-based) - Inscript

		   Tamil (Encoding-based) - ISCII
		   Hindi (Encoding-based) - ISCII

The above supports are complete. (This simply means that we have populated
the appropriate language dependent parse rule files). We are currently
working on Malayalam, Oriya, Marathi and Gujarathi.

Future Plans: This work is part of a major plan to develop a multimodal
interface to the computer.  By multimodal, we mean, handwriting, keyboard
and speech interfaces.  We have started work on both handwriting and speech. 
We have developed a handwriting interface for Tamil and have developed
speech technology software for: speech synthesis in Hindi, Tamil, Telugu and
Malayalam (Malayalam database was obtained from ISDL, Trivandrum); spoken
language identification, syllable-based recognition of continuous speech,
speaker identification. (ENDS)

From ragu at vsnl.com  Fri Dec 27 15:42:00 2002
From: ragu at vsnl.com (Raghavendra Bhat)
Date: Fri, 27 Dec 2002 21:12:00 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] Mirroring Deb packages! ==> Great job
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0212271136440.2458-100000@Uday.bksys.co.in>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0212271136440.2458-100000@Uday.bksys.co.in>
Message-ID: <20021227154200.GA821@gnuhead>

[Do not pine for `non-free' stuff]

Udaya posts:

>> if you guys  have any tool to evaulate the  best mirror, please let
>> me know.

`apt-get install apt-spy'

Downloads from debian.org a list  of current mirrors and tests each of
the mirrors for bandwidth.   Writes a /etc/apt/sources.list file based
on the responses it gets.  (blatant cut & paste job :)

Also install iftop and watch the juice flowing..... 


>> i  do have  the deb  woody 3.0  cds, so  i think  i could  copy the
>> binaries from that, and start mirroring

Eg. to update  CD-1 of woody from 3.0r0 to 3.0r1,  read on, repeat for
the other CDs.

Do a  dd and create the  image, mount this  image at /loop by  doing a

`mount -o loop debian-30r0-i386-binary-1_NONUS.iso /loop'
`apt-get install jigdo-file'  

As su,  run `jigdo-lite' from  within the dir  where you have  the iso
image of  CD-1 and care should be  taken to free up  ample space here.
Read    the    docs   at    (http://home.in.tum.de/~atterer/jigdo/).
Articulate your problems, if any, and we shall help. 

Best....

From smohan at vsnl.com  Sat Dec 28 02:11:54 2002
From: smohan at vsnl.com (S Mohan)
Date: Sat, 28 Dec 2002 07:41:54 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] root passwd
In-Reply-To: <20021227131911.GB17665@cmi.ac.in>
Message-ID: <002901c2ae16$800a2fe0$c16041db@18yamuna>

I've seen specific boot floppies on the Net that help you reset root
password. In case you cannot get it, just download tomsrtbt. It creates
a boot floppy and on boot copies (expands rather) the full filesystems
into ramdisk and operates out of ramdisk. You can then mount your root
partition, edit the /etc/passwd and/or /etc/shadow file, remove the
password and boot. No password will be asked. Change the password then
after boot.

Mohan

-----Original Message-----
From: ilugc-admin@aero.iitm.ernet.in

Sent: Friday, December 27, 2002 6:49 PM
To: ILUGC
Subject: Re: [Ilugc] root passwd


Hi,

	You may not always land up at the root prompt!

	By default GNU/Linux/Debian (let me be safe) systems start up 
slogin and not bash. Which means you need root password to boot into 
single user mode.

	If single user mode fails, then you may try using a rescue
floppy. Or an installation CD-Rom (choose rescue mode).

	Well, there's another neat way to do it by using the other
kernel 
parameters! Go ahead and read the docs to find out!

if you wanted to just disable  the bell OR have a visible notification
of your bell, you can put the line:
set bell-style visible
    OR
set bell-style none

in  your .inputrc  (this wil  work  only if  your shell  uses the  GNU
Readline  Library. GNU Bash  is one  such shell).  info bash  for more
details on playing with .inputrc :)

From itmani at hotmail.com  Sat Dec 28 15:55:34 2002
From: itmani at hotmail.com (Manikandan P.)
Date: Sat, 28 Dec 2002 09:55:34 -0600
Subject: [Ilugc] .inputrc tricks
References: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0212261424100.631-100000@lantana.iitm.ernet.in> <001301c2acc8$e5060990$0201a8c0@quirk> <20021227130948.GA17665@cmi.ac.in> <20021228034046.GD25298@symonds.net>
Message-ID: <OE52LcKkPQh0pIYW51X00004484@hotmail.com>

hi luggies


>info bash  for more details on playing with .inputrc :)
fun with .inputrc
add the following lines to your .inputrc

"\e[11~":"ps -e\C-M"
"\e[12~":"ls\C-M"
"\e[13~":"cd ..\C-M"
"\e[14~":"pwd\C-M"

the above maps frequently used commands like ps,ls,cd ..,pwd to F1,F2,F3,F4
Functions keys
e.g
"key-sequence":"command"

Happy hacking.....
Manikandan P.

From mvikyk at yahoo.co.uk  Sat Dec 28 09:30:05 2002
From: mvikyk at yahoo.co.uk (vignesh)
Date: Sat, 28 Dec 2002 15:00:05 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] Display problems in 845/850 chipset
In-Reply-To: <OF5A243282.A548350D-ON65256C9C.0015F0EA@polaris.co.in>
References: <OF5A243282.A548350D-ON65256C9C.0015F0EA@polaris.co.in>
Message-ID: <200212281500.05811.mvikyk@yahoo.co.uk>

Hi,

With reference to the display problems in 845/850 chipset problem posted two 
days ago, I thank Mr. Prabu<prabuanand@softhome.net> for letting me know the 
solution.  I am forwarding his mail, so that it might be useful for the needy 
ones.

His mail reads thus:

**************************************************************************************
"Visit http://www.intel.com/support/graphics/intel845g/linux.htm

Here is the page FYI

Do the Intel Extreme Graphics Drivers Support Linux*? 

Linux* graphics driver availability
 Intel Extreme Graphics drivers for Linux* are not available for download from 
Intel. Linux* drivers for the Intel 82845G graphics controller have been 
released for distribution to interested parties and directly to the XFree86* 
 website. Future releases of most Linux distributions should contain native 
Intel 82845G graphics controller support. For information on the supported 
graphics adapters for your version of XFree86, please check the documentation 
for your version of XFree86 or the documentation for the Linux distribution.

 If your version of Linux does not have native Intel 82845G graphics 
controller support, the VESA driver that comes with XFree86* can be used. To 
use the VESA driver, modify the /etc/X11/XF86Config-4 file and change the 
driver line to:

 
Section "Device"
 ...
 Driver "vesa"
 ...
EndSection
Legacy video memory reserved by the BIOS
 Both the VESA driver and the native graphics driver for Linux use the legacy 
video memory allocated by the BIOS for display. Because of this, it is 
important that the BIOS allocate 8 MB of video memory to allow a full range 
of video mode support. Check your system or motherboard documentation on how 
to determine and possibly adjust the amount of pre-allocated video memory. On 
Intel Desktop Boards, the setting is found in the BIOS setup under Advanced 
> Video Configuration > Frame Buffer Size.

 If your motherboard or laptop is limited to 1MB of legacy video memory and 
does not allow adjustment of this size in the BIOS setup, currently the only 
way to correct the issue is for the motherboard or laptop vendor to release a 
BIOS update. Intel Desktop Boards ship with the BIOS options of 512K, 1MB, or 
8MB for legacy video. At this time, there is no driver available from Intel 
to overcome the legacy VGA memory limitation.

Commercial Linux graphics drivers
A commercial provider of 3D accelerated drivers for Linux is available, but 
these drivers are not free of charge. Xi Graphics* has developed these 
drivers without involvement from Intel and these drivers are only mentioned 
here as a courtesy by Intel as an alternative proposal for interested 
parties. Intel does not support drivers from other vendors, and Intel does 
not warrant and cannot be responsible in any way for the content or operation 
of these drivers. 
XiG 

Additional Linux updates for the chipset
 The following additional, non-graphics related Linux updates are available to 
enable other chipset features: 
Intel 845G chipset family integrated audio 
Intel 845G chipset family ATA DMA support"
***************************************************************************

I followed the above procedure and I got the display up properly.  Still, I 
had to make a few more changes using #xf86config.  Namely, since the 
motherboard (Intel 845 original) took away 32MB of Ram as shared memory, I 
entered video card memory as 32768K, instead of default 8MB. Further, I had 
to enter 'n' explicitly for the question "Do you want to have the screen 
bigger than the physical screen?".   If this is not done, I was able to see 
only 1/4th of the full screen.

I thank everyone for the help offered.

c u /

The issue is that you have clearly not read either

1. The sendmail faq

From smohan at vsnl.com  Mon Dec 30 07:56:17 2002
From: smohan at vsnl.com (S Mohan)
Date: Mon, 30 Dec 2002 13:26:17 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] Unable to telnet port 25 on local machine
In-Reply-To: <000201c2afd4$8e214db0$ccd4b2c6@hclbb>
Message-ID: <JIEJJMCEIMFADEIEBHOCCEMDDBAA.smohan@vsnl.com>

telnet is invoked by xinetd. Access to this is governed by a file telnet in
/etc/xinetd directory where in disabled would be marked yes. Change it to
no. If this still does not work, check the hosts.allow and hosts.deny file
in /etc where IP masks may have been denied.

Mohan
