On Monday, December 30, 2002 1:26 PM [GMT+0530=IST],
smohan@vsnl.com (S Mohan) wrote:

> telnet is invoked by xinetd. Access to this is governed by a file
> telnet in /etc/xinetd directory where in disabled would be marked
> yes. Change it to no. If this still does not work, check the
> hosts.allow and hosts.deny file in /etc where IP masks may have been
> denied.

The issue is not that he is unable to telnet (aka port 23) - where your
advice would be correct.

The issue is that he can do (forget the word telnet, as it seems to
confuse the issue, try, say, netcat) -

$ nc localhost 25

but not

$ nc his.host.name 25

or

$ nc his.public.ip 25

    srs

From smohan at vsnl.com  Mon Dec 30 09:18:51 2002
From: smohan at vsnl.com (S Mohan)
Date: Mon, 30 Dec 2002 14:48:51 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] Unable to telnet port 25 on local machine
In-Reply-To: <061301c2afda$e4b89ab0$0201a8c0@quirk>
Message-ID: <JIEJJMCEIMFADEIEBHOCEEMGDBAA.smohan@vsnl.com>

Oops missed that one. It is the SMTP IP address listening that needs to be
set. In sendmail.cf the "O DaemonPortOptions=Name=MTA" is by default set to
localhost or 127.0.0.1. Set it to the specific IP or remove 127.0.0.1.

Mohan

From mallet at efn.org  Mon Dec 30 10:34:53 2002
From: mallet at efn.org (Suresh Ramasubramanian)
Date: Mon, 30 Dec 2002 16:04:53 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] Unable to telnet port 25 on local machine
References: <JIEJJMCEIMFADEIEBHOCEEMGDBAA.smohan@vsnl.com>
Message-ID: <007401c2afef$d623f340$0201a8c0@quirk>

On Monday, December 30, 2002 2:48 PM [GMT+0530=IST],
smohan@vsnl.com (S Mohan) wrote:

> Oops missed that one. It is the SMTP IP address listening that needs
> to be set. In sendmail.cf the "O DaemonPortOptions=Name=MTA" is by
> default set to localhost or 127.0.0.1. Set it to the specific IP or
> remove 127.0.0.1.

That would leave sendmail listening on your public IP but not on
localhost.

Actually, best not to fiddle with sendmail.cf - just remove the
DAEMON_OPTIONS line pointing to 127.0.0.1 from sendmail.mc and rebuild
sendmail.cf

    srs

From ragu at vsnl.com  Tue Dec 31 04:23:43 2002
From: ragu at vsnl.com (Raghavendra Bhat)
Date: Tue, 31 Dec 2002 09:53:43 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] Tool to create databse in linux
In-Reply-To: <20021230171914.7207.qmail@webmail9.rediffmail.com>
References: <20021230171914.7207.qmail@webmail9.rediffmail.com>
Message-ID: <20021231042343.GA6838@gnuhead>

durairaj posts :

>> can anyone tell me whether any tool is available to create database
>> in linux..
      ^^^^^

Linux is  the kernel and people  mistakenly say that the  OS is Linux.
The system is the GNU/Linux system, can we call an apple an orange ?

There is no such tool to create databases for the kernel Linux per se.
But for the  GNU/Linux system, there are many  `free' tools to create,
administer and design  database schemas.  The choice is  varied in that
you may  get confused  selecting one.  I  have found  Postgresql quite
robust and easy to learn.  Read this link and come to your conclusions
http://www.fokus.gmd.de/linux/HOWTO/PostgreSQL-HOWTO.html

This FAQ on Postgresql is also helpful and extremely readable
http://postgresql.linux.cz/docs/faq-english.html

There was this comparison on LinuxPlanet a while ago
//www.linuxplanet.com/linuxplanet/tutorials/1224/1/

Best of regards.
-- 
ragOO, Freedom of the Air Waves, GNU Radio
The GNU Project  ::    http://www.gnu.org/
Free Software  is not   `free masala dosa'
Free Software  is about computing freedom.

From mssnlayam at cs.annauniv.edu  Mon Dec 30 15:27:10 2002
From: mssnlayam at cs.annauniv.edu (Suriya Narayanan M S)
Date: Mon, 30 Dec 2002 20:57:10 +0530
Subject: [Ilugc] inode
In-Reply-To: <20021230130731.14702.qmail@web10304.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20021230130731.14702.qmail@web10304.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <200212312354.gBVNs6MC004041@cs.annauniv.edu>

On Monday 30 December 2002 18:37, you wrote:
> Well I am sad to write this from a win98 machine bcaz
> of stupid command -> "dd if=111.bin of=/dev/hda2
> bs=1440 count=1"
> from root on RH 7.1
> Actually /dev/hda2 was where / got mounted
> everytime..but now this
> command has caused inode table to get corrupted on
> /dev/hda2
> (may be bcaz i replaced usual bs=512 to bs=1440 and so
> its written to
> unwanted space cauing damage to i-node tables)..
> now i can't go beyond kernel panic screen on RH 7.1
> So Can i get back my data in /dev/hda2 ???How?
> Pls mail me personally and forward this to known Sys
> Admins
I am assuming that the filesystem is ext2 or ext3, and
access is available to  a computer running GNU and
the harddisk can be fitted there

If the dd command was invoked exactly as above, then
only 1440 bytes are lost. The first 512 bytes form the boot
sector. So only (1440 - 512)  928 bytes are lost.
The ext2 filesystem maintains several alternative copies
of the superblock. Run the e2fsck program by specifying
an alternative superblock.

Another solution would be to use dd again. Copy an
alternate superblock to the original superblock.
(Please back up the partition, and read the ext2 filesystem
format before doing this)

I am mailing this to the group so that someone might correct
in case I am wrong.
